<p><b>University College London</b> (<b>UCL</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Constituent_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituent college">constituent college</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_university" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal university">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>. It is the third largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_enrolment" title="List of universities in the United Kingdom by enrolment">university in the United Kingdom by total enrolment</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HESA_citation_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HESA_citation-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the largest by postgraduate enrolment.
</p><p>Established in 1826 as <b>London University</b> by founders inspired by the radical ideas of <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bentham" title="Jeremy Bentham">Jeremy Bentham</a>, UCL was the first university institution to be established in London, and the first in England to be entirely secular and to admit students regardless of their religion.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> UCL also makes the contested claims of being the <a href="/wiki/Third_oldest_university_in_England_debate" class="mw-redirect" title="Third oldest university in England debate">third-oldest university in England</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> and the first to admit women.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup> In 1836 UCL became one of the two founding <a href="/wiki/Colleges_of_the_University_of_London" title="Colleges of the University of London">colleges of the University of London</a>, which was granted a royal charter in the same year. It has grown through mergers, including with the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Neurology" title="UCL Institute of Neurology">Institute of Neurology</a> (in 1997), the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Free_Hospital" title="Royal Free Hospital">Royal Free Hospital</a> Medical School (in 1998), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Eastman_Dental_Institute" title="UCL Eastman Dental Institute">Eastman Dental Institute</a> (in 1999), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">School of Slavonic and East European Studies</a> (in 1999), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Pharmacy" title="UCL School of Pharmacy">School of Pharmacy</a> (in 2012) and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Education" title="UCL Institute of Education">Institute of Education</a> (in 2014).
</p><p>UCL has its main campus in the <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury" title="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">central London</a>, with a number of institutes and teaching hospitals elsewhere in central London and satellite campuses in <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Olympic_Park" title="Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park">Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stratford,_London" title="Stratford, London">Stratford</a>, east London and in <a href="/wiki/Doha,_Qatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Doha, Qatar">Doha, Qatar</a>. UCL is organised into <a href="/wiki/University_College_London#Faculties_and_departments" title="University College London">11 constituent faculties</a>, within which there are over 100 departments, institutes and research centres. UCL operates several culturally significant museums and manages collections in a wide range of fields, including the <a href="/wiki/Petrie_Museum_of_Egyptian_Archaeology" title="Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology">Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grant_Museum_of_Zoology_and_Comparative_Anatomy" title="Grant Museum of Zoology and Comparative Anatomy">Grant Museum of Zoology and Comparative Anatomy</a>, and administers the annual <a href="/wiki/Orwell_Prize" title="Orwell Prize">Orwell Prize</a> in political writing. In 2016/17, UCL had around 37,900 students and 14,600 staff (including around 7,100 academic staff and 840 professors) and had a total group income of £1.33 billion, of which £459.8 million was from research grants and contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the most recent <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a> rankings for research power, UCL was the top-rated university in the UK as calculated by <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and second as calculated by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>/<i><a href="/wiki/Research_Fortnight" title="Research Fortnight">Research Fortnight</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> UCL had the 9th highest average entry tariff in the UK for students starting in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Globally, UCL is ranked from tenth to twentieth in the four major international rankings,<sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2017_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2017-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CWTS_Leiden_Ranking_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CWTS_Leiden_Ranking-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QS_World_University_Rankings_2019_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS_World_University_Rankings_2019-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THE_World_University_Rankings_2017-18_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_World_University_Rankings_2017-18-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and from eighth to eleventh in the <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">national league tables</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2019_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2019-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2018_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2018-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> UCL is a member of numerous academic organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>, and is part of <a href="/wiki/UCL_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Partners">UCL Partners</a>, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Academic_health_science_centre" title="Academic health science centre">academic health science centre</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Health_Service_Journal_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_Service_Journal-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_triangle_(universities)" title="Golden triangle (universities)">golden triangle</a>" of research-intensive English universities.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL alumni include the '<a href="/wiki/Father_of_the_Nation" title="Father of the Nation">Father of the Nation</a>' of each of India, Kenya and Mauritius, the founders of Ghana, modern Japan and Nigeria, the inventor of the telephone, and one of the co-discoverers of the structure of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>. UCL academics discovered five of the naturally occurring <a href="/wiki/Noble_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Noble gases">noble gases</a>, discovered <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">hormones</a>, invented the <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_tube" title="Vacuum tube">vacuum tube</a>, and made several <a href="/wiki/History_of_statistics" title="History of statistics">foundational advances</a> in modern statistics. As of 2017, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_University_College_London" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with University College London">33 Nobel Prize winners</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fields_Medal_winners_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Fields Medal winners by university affiliation">3 Fields medalists</a> have been affiliated with UCL as alumni, faculty or researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
