<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_University_College_London" title="History of University College London">History of University College London</a></div>
<h3><span id="1826_to_1836_.E2.80.93_London_University"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1826_to_1836_–_London_University">1826 to 1836 – London University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1826 to 1836 – London University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG/220px-The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG/330px-The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG/440px-The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG 2x" data-file-width="484" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_London_University_by_Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd_1827-28.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The London University</i> as drawn by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hosmer_Shepherd" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Hosmer Shepherd">Thomas Hosmer Shepherd</a> and published in 1827–1828 (now the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Main_Building" title="UCL Main Building">UCL Main Building</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>UCL was founded on 11 February 1826 under the name London University, as an alternative to the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> universities of Oxford and Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Penman_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penman-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> London University's first Warden was <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Horner" title="Leonard Horner">Leonard Horner</a>, who was the first scientist to head a British university.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG/170px-Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG/255px-Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG/340px-Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1454" data-file-height="1947" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Four_founders_of_UCL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_Tonks" title="Henry Tonks">Henry Tonks</a>' 1923 mural <i>The Four Founders of UCL</i></div></div></div>
<p>Despite the commonly held belief that the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bentham" title="Jeremy Bentham">Jeremy Bentham</a> was the founder of UCL, his direct involvement was limited to the purchase of share No. 633, at a cost of £100 paid in nine instalments between December 1826 and January 1830. In 1828 he did nominate a friend to sit on the council, and in 1827 attempted to have his disciple <a href="/wiki/John_Bowring" title="John Bowring">John Bowring</a> appointed as the first professor of English or History, but on both occasions his candidates were unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This suggests that while his ideas may have been influential, he himself was less so. However, Bentham is today commonly regarded as the "spiritual father" of UCL, as his radical ideas on education and society were the inspiration to the institution's founders, particularly the Scotsmen <a href="/wiki/James_Mill" title="James Mill">James Mill</a> (1773–1836) and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Brougham,_1st_Baron_Brougham_and_Vaux" title="Henry Brougham, 1st Baron Brougham and Vaux">Henry Brougham</a> (1778–1868).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1827, the Chair of Political Economy at London University was created, with <a href="/wiki/John_Ramsay_McCulloch" title="John Ramsay McCulloch">John Ramsay McCulloch</a> as the first incumbent, establishing one of the first departments of economics in England.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1828 the university became the first in England to offer English as a subject<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and the teaching of Classics and medicine began. In 1830, London University founded the London University School, which would later become <a href="/wiki/University_College_School" title="University College School">University College School</a>. In 1833, the university appointed <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Maconochie_(penal_reformer)" title="Alexander Maconochie (penal reformer)">Alexander Maconochie</a>, Secretary to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Geographical_Society" title="Royal Geographical Society">Royal Geographical Society</a>, as the first professor of geography in the UK. In 1834, <a href="/wiki/University_College_Hospital" title="University College Hospital">University College Hospital</a> (originally North London Hospital) opened as a teaching hospital for the university's medical school.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1836_to_1900_.E2.80.93_University_College.2C_London"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1836_to_1900_–_University_College,_London">1836 to 1900 – University College, London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1836 to 1900 – University College, London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1836, London University was incorporated by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> under the name <i>University College, London</i>. On the same day, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> was created by royal charter as a degree-awarding examining board for students from affiliated schools and colleges, with University College and <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King's College, London</a> being named in the charter as the first two affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Slade_School_of_Fine_Art" title="Slade School of Fine Art">Slade School of Fine Art</a> was founded as part of University College in 1871, following a bequest from <a href="/wiki/Felix_Slade" title="Felix Slade">Felix Slade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1878, the University of London gained a supplemental charter making it the first British university to be allowed to award degrees to women. The same year, UCL admitted women to the faculties of Arts and Law and of Science, although women remained barred from the faculties of Engineering and of Medicine (with the exception of courses on public health and hygiene).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> While UCL claims to have been the first university in England to admit women on equal terms to men, from 1878, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bristol" title="University of Bristol">University of Bristol</a> also makes this claim, having admitted women from its foundation (as a college) in 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Armstrong College, a predecessor institution of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a>, also allowed women to enter from its foundation in 1871, although none actually enrolled until 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Women were finally admitted to medical studies during the First World War in 1917, although after the war ended limitations were placed on their numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Ramsay_working.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/William_Ramsay_working.jpg/170px-William_Ramsay_working.jpg" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/William_Ramsay_working.jpg/255px-William_Ramsay_working.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/William_Ramsay_working.jpg/340px-William_Ramsay_working.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1226" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Ramsay_working.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Ramsay" title="William Ramsay">William Ramsay</a> is regarded as the "<i>father of noble gases</i>".</div></div></div>
<p>In 1898, <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Ramsay" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir William Ramsay">Sir William Ramsay</a> discovered the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_element" title="Chemical element">elements</a> <a href="/wiki/Krypton" title="Krypton">krypton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neon" title="Neon">neon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xenon" title="Xenon">xenon</a> whilst professor of chemistry at UCL.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1900_to_1976_.E2.80.93_University_of_London.2C_University_College"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1900_to_1976_–_University_of_London,_University_College">1900 to 1976 – University of London, University College</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1900 to 1976 – University of London, University College">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1900, the University of London was reconstituted as a federal university with new statutes drawn up under the University of London Act 1898. UCL, along with a number of other colleges in London, became a school of the University of London. While most of the constituent institutions retained their autonomy, UCL was merged into the University in 1907 under the University College London (Transfer) Act 1905 and lost its legal independence.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>1900 also saw the decision to appoint a salaried head of the college. The first incumbent was <a href="/wiki/Carey_Foster" title="Carey Foster">Carey Foster</a>, who served as <a href="/wiki/Principal_(academia)" title="Principal (academia)">Principal</a> (as the post was originally titled) from 1900 to 1904. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Foster" title="Gregory Foster">Gregory Foster</a> (no relation), and in 1906 the title was changed to <a href="/wiki/Provost_(education)" title="Provost (education)">Provost</a> to avoid confusion with the Principal of the University of London. Gregory Foster remained in post until 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 1906, the Cruciform Building was opened as the new home for <a href="/wiki/University_College_Hospital" title="University College Hospital">University College Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL sustained considerable bomb damage during the Second World War, including to the Great Hall and the Carey Foster Physics Laboratory. The first UCL student magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/Pi_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Pi Magazine">Pi Magazine</a></i>, was published for the first time on 21 February 1946. The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Jewish_Studies_at_University_College_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Jewish Studies at University College London">Institute of Jewish Studies</a> relocated to UCL in 1959.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mullard_Space_Science_Laboratory" title="Mullard Space Science Laboratory">Mullard Space Science Laboratory</a> was established in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 1973, UCL became the first international node to the precursor of the internet, the ARPANET.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although UCL was among the first universities to admit women on the same terms as men, in 1878, the college's senior common room, the Housman Room, remained men-only until 1969. After two unsuccessful attempts, a motion was passed that ended segregation by sex at UCL. This was achieved by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Woledge" title="Brian Woledge">Brian Woledge</a> (Fielden Professor of French at UCL from 1939 to 1971) and <a href="/wiki/David_Colquhoun" title="David Colquhoun">David Colquhoun</a>, at that time a young lecturer in pharmacology.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1976_to_2005">1976 to 2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1976 to 2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Portico_and_steps,_University_College,_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg" class="image"><img alt="UCL" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg/200px-Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg" width="200" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg/300px-Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg/400px-Portico_and_steps%2C_University_College%2C_London_-_geograph.org.uk_-_364428.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="497" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Wilkins Building in 1956</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Wilkins_Building_1,_UCL,_London_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="UCL" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg/200px-Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg" width="200" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg/300px-Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg/400px-Wilkins_Building_1%2C_UCL%2C_London_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2636" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Today</div></div></div></div>
<p>In 1976, a new charter restored UCL's legal independence, although still without the power to award its own degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Under this charter the college became formally known as University College London, having previously formally been "University of London, University College" since its incorporation into the University. This name abandoned the comma used in its earlier name of "University College, London".
</p><p>In 1986, UCL merged with the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Archaeology" title="UCL Institute of Archaeology">Institute of Archaeology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guard221002_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard221002-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In 1988, UCL merged with the Institute of Laryngology &amp; Otology, the Institute of Orthopaedics, the Institute of Urology &amp; Nephrology and <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_Hospital" title="Middlesex Hospital">Middlesex Hospital Medical School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guard221002_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard221002-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1993, a reorganisation of the University of London meant that UCL and other colleges gained direct access to government funding and the right to confer University of London degrees themselves. This led to UCL being regarded as a <i>de facto</i> university in its own right.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, the <a href="/wiki/University_College_London_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">University College London Hospitals NHS Trust</a> was established.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> UCL merged with the College of Speech Sciences and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Ophthalmology" title="UCL Institute of Ophthalmology">Institute of Ophthalmology</a> in 1995, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Child_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Institute of Child Health">Institute of Child Health</a> and the School of Podiatry in 1996<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Neurology" title="UCL Institute of Neurology">Institute of Neurology</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-guard221002_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard221002-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, UCL merged with the Royal Free Hospital Medical School to create the Royal Free and University College Medical School (renamed the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Medical_School" title="UCL Medical School">UCL Medical School</a> in October 2008). In 1999, UCL merged with the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">School of Slavonic and East European Studies</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Eastman_Dental_Institute" title="UCL Eastman Dental Institute">Eastman Dental Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guard221002_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard221002-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/UCL_Jill_Dando_Institute" title="UCL Jill Dando Institute">UCL Jill Dando Institute of Crime Science</a>, the first university department in the world devoted specifically to reducing crime, was founded in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Proposals for a merger between UCL and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a> were announced in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The proposal provoked strong opposition from UCL teaching staff and students and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_University_Teachers" title="Association of University Teachers">AUT union</a>, which criticised "the indecent haste and lack of consultation", leading to its abandonment by the UCL Provost Sir <a href="/wiki/Derek_Roberts" title="Derek Roberts">Derek Roberts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The blogs that helped to stop the merger are preserved, though some of the links are now broken: see David Colquhoun's blog<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and the Save UCL blog,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> which was run by David Conway, a postgraduate student in the department of Hebrew and Jewish studies.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/London_Centre_for_Nanotechnology" title="London Centre for Nanotechnology">London Centre for Nanotechnology</a> was established in 2003 as a joint venture between UCL and Imperial College London.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2003, when UCL Professor <a href="/wiki/David_Latchman" title="David Latchman">David Latchman</a> became Master of the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Birkbeck,_University_of_London" title="Birkbeck, University of London">Birkbeck</a>, he has forged closer relations between these two University of London colleges, and personally maintains departments at both. Joint research centres include the UCL/Birkbeck Institute for Earth and Planetary Sciences, the UCL/Birkbeck/<a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Education">IoE</a> Centre for Educational Neuroscience, the UCL/Birkbeck Institute of Structural and Molecular Biology, and the Birkbeck-UCL Centre for Neuroimaging.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005_to_2010">2005 to 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2005 to 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg/220px-School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg/330px-School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg/440px-School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2447" data-file-height="2492" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies</a> building, which was opened in 2005</div></div></div>
<p>In 2005, UCL was finally granted its own taught and research degree awarding powers and all UCL students registered from 2007/08 qualified with UCL degrees. Also in 2005, UCL adopted a new corporate branding under which the name University College London was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Acronym_and_initialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Acronym and initialism">initialism</a> UCL in all external communications.<sup id="cite_ref-Baty_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baty-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In the same year, a major new £422 million building was opened for University College Hospital on <a href="/wiki/Euston_Road" title="Euston Road">Euston Road</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Ear_Institute" title="UCL Ear Institute">UCL Ear Institute</a> was established and a new building for the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies</a> was opened.
</p><p>In 2007, the UCL Cancer Institute was opened in the newly constructed Paul O'Gorman Building. In August 2008, UCL formed <a href="/wiki/UCL_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Partners">UCL Partners</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Academic_health_science_centre" title="Academic health science centre">academic health science centre</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital_for_Children_NHS_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children NHS Trust">Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children NHS Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moorfields_Eye_Hospital_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Moorfields Eye Hospital NHS Foundation Trust">Moorfields Eye Hospital NHS Foundation Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Free_London_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Royal Free London NHS Foundation Trust">Royal Free London NHS Foundation Trust</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_College_London_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uclpartners_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclpartners-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, UCL established the UCL School of Energy &amp; Resources in Adelaide, Australia, the first campus of a British university in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The School was based in the historic <a href="/wiki/Torrens_Building" title="Torrens Building">Torrens Building</a> in Victoria Square and its creation followed negotiations between UCL Vice Provost Michael Worton and South Australian Premier Mike Rann.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, the Yale UCL Collaborative was established between UCL, <a href="/wiki/UCL_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Partners">UCL Partners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_School_of_Medicine" title="Yale School of Medicine">Yale School of Medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_%E2%80%93_New_Haven_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Yale – New Haven Hospital">Yale – New Haven Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest collaboration in the history of either university, and its scope has subsequently been extended to the humanities and social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_to_2015">2010 to 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010 to 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torrens_Building,_Victoria_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg/170px-Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg/255px-Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg/340px-Torrens_Building%2C_Victoria_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torrens_Building,_Victoria_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Torrens Building in <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a>, which housed the UCL School of Energy and Resources</div></div></div>
<p>In June 2011, the mining company <a href="/wiki/BHP_Billiton" class="mw-redirect" title="BHP Billiton">BHP Billiton</a> agreed to donate AU$10 million to UCL to fund the establishment of two energy institutes – the Energy Policy Institute, based in Adelaide, and the Institute for Sustainable Resources, based in London.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2011, UCL announced plans for a £500 million investment in its main Bloomsbury campus over 10 years, as well as the establishment of a new 23-acre campus next to the Olympic Park in Stratford in the East End of London.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It revised its plans of expansion in East London and in December 2014 announced to build a campus (UCL East) covering 11 acres and provide up to 125,000m<sup>2</sup> of space on <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Olympic_Park" title="Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park">Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> UCL East will be part of plans to transform the Olympic Park into a cultural and innovation hub, where UCL will open its first school of design, a centre of experimental engineering and a museum of the future, along with a living space for students.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/School_of_Pharmacy,_University_of_London" class="mw-redirect" title="School of Pharmacy, University of London">School of Pharmacy, University of London</a> merged with UCL on 1 January 2012, becoming the UCL School of Pharmacy within the Faculty of Life Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In May 2012, UCL, Imperial College London and the semiconductor company <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> announced the establishment of the Intel Collaborative Research Institute for Sustainable Connected Cities, a London-based institute for research into the future of cities.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2012, UCL received criticism for advertising an unpaid research position; it subsequently withdrew the advert.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL and the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Education">Institute of Education</a> formed a strategic alliance in October 2012, including co-operation in teaching, research and the development of the London schools system.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In February 2014, the two institutions announced their intention to merge,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and the merger was completed in December 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2013, a new Department of Science, Technology, Engineering and Public Policy (STEaPP) was established within the Faculty of Engineering, one of several initiatives within the university to increase and reflect upon the links between research and public sector decision-making.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2013, it was announced that the Translation Studies Unit of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a> would move to UCL, becoming part of the UCL School of European Languages, Culture and Society.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> In December 2013, it was announced that UCL and the academic publishing company <a href="/wiki/Elsevier" title="Elsevier">Elsevier</a> would collaborate to establish the UCL Big Data Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In January 2015, it was announced that UCL had been selected by the UK government as one of the five founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing_Institute" title="Alan Turing Institute">Alan Turing Institute</a> (together with the universities of Cambridge, Edinburgh, Oxford and Warwick), an institute to be established at the British Library to promote the development and use of advanced mathematics, computer science, algorithms and <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_to_present">2015 to present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2015 to present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Londres_097..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Londres_097..jpg/170px-Londres_097..jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Londres_097..jpg/255px-Londres_097..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Londres_097..jpg/340px-Londres_097..jpg 2x" data-file-width="692" data-file-height="922" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Londres_097..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Management" title="UCL School of Management">UCL School of Management</a> is located at Level 38, <a href="/wiki/One_Canada_Square" title="One Canada Square">One Canada Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a></div></div></div>
<p>In August 2015, the Department of Management Science and Innovation was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Management" title="UCL School of Management">School of Management</a> and plans were announced to greatly expand UCL's activities in the area of business-related teaching and research.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The School is currently being moved from the Bloomsbury campus to <a href="/wiki/One_Canada_Square" title="One Canada Square">One Canada Square</a> in Canary Wharf.
</p><p>UCL established the Institute of Advanced Studies (IAS) in 2015 to promote interdisciplinary research in humanities and social sciences. The prestigious annual <a href="/wiki/Orwell_Prize" title="Orwell Prize">Orwell Prize</a> for political writing moved to the IAS in 2016.
</p><p>In June 2016 it was reported in the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> that as a result of administrative errors hundreds of students who studied at the UCL Eastman Dental Institute between 2005–6 and 2013–14 had been given the wrong marks, leading to an unknown number of students being attributed with the wrong qualifications and, in some cases, being failed when they should have passed their degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-THE7716_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE7716-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> A report by UCL’s Academic Committee Review Panel noted that, according to the Institute’s own review findings, senior members of UCL staff had been aware of issues affecting students' results but had not taken action to address them.<sup id="cite_ref-UCLAC1213_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLAC1213-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The Review Panel concluded that there had been an apparent lack of ownership of these matters amongst the Institute’s senior staff.<sup id="cite_ref-UCLAC1213_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLAC1213-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2016 it was announced that UCL would be the hub institution for a new £250 million national dementia research institute, to be funded with £150 million from the <a href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(United_Kingdom)" title="Medical Research Council (United Kingdom)">Medical Research Council</a> and £50 million each from <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_Research_UK" title="Alzheimer&#39;s Research UK">Alzheimer's Research UK</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_Society" title="Alzheimer&#39;s Society">Alzheimer's Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2017 it was reported that staff morale was at "an all time low", with 68% of members of the academic board who responded to a survey disagreeing with the statement "UCL is well managed" and 86% with "the teaching facilities are adequate for the number of students". Michael Arthur, the Provost and President, linked the results to the "major change programme" at UCL. He admitted that facilities were under pressure following growth over the past decade, but said that the issues were being addressed through the development of UCL East and rental of other additional space.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2017 UCL's council voted to apply for university status while remaining part of the University of London.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> UCL's application to become a university is subject to parliament passing a bill to amend the statutes of the University of London, which is, as of July 2018, held up by procedural issues in the House of Commons.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UCL Adelaide satellite campus closed in December 2017, with academic staff and student transferring to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Australia" title="University of South Australia">University of South Australia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, UCL opened <i>UCL at Here East</i>, at the Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park, offering courses jointly between the <a href="/wiki/The_Bartlett" title="The Bartlett">Bartlett Faculty of the Built Environment</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Faculty_of_Engineering_Sciences" title="UCL Faculty of Engineering Sciences">Faculty of Engineering Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_East_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_East-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The campus offers a variety of undergraduate and postgraduate master's degrees,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> with the first undergraduate students, on a new Engineering and Architectural Design <a href="/wiki/MEng" class="mw-redirect" title="MEng">MEng</a>, starting in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> It was announced in August 2018 that a £215 million contract for construction of the largest building in the <i>UCL East</i> development, Marshgate 1, had been awarded to <a href="/wiki/Mace_(construction_company)" title="Mace (construction company)">Mace</a>, with building to begin in 2019 and be completed by 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_and_locations">Campus and locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Campus and locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Bloomsbury">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Filming_at_UCL" class="mw-redirect" title="Filming at UCL">Filming at UCL</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg/220px-University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg/330px-University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg/440px-University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3132" data-file-height="2447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_London_-quadrant-11Sept2006_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Wilkins Building and main quadrangle</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rockefeller_Building,_UCL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg/220px-Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg/330px-Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg/440px-Rockefeller_Building%2C_UCL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rockefeller_Building,_UCL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Rockefeller Building on University Street, one of UCL's largest premises</div></div></div>
<p>UCL is primarily based in the <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury" title="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</a> area of the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">London Borough of Camden</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">Central London</a>. The main campus is located around <a href="/wiki/Gower_Street_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gower Street (London)">Gower Street</a> and includes the biology, chemistry, economics, engineering, geography, history, languages, mathematics, management, philosophy and physics departments, the preclinical facilities of the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Medical_School" title="UCL Medical School">UCL Medical School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_Centre_for_Nanotechnology" title="London Centre for Nanotechnology">London Centre for Nanotechnology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Slade_School_of_Fine_Art" title="Slade School of Fine Art">Slade School of Fine Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Union">UCL Union</a>, the main UCL Library, the UCL Science Library, the <a href="/wiki/The_UCL_Bloomsbury" class="mw-redirect" title="The UCL Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Petrie_Museum_of_Egyptian_Archaeology" title="Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology">Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grant_Museum_of_Zoology" class="mw-redirect" title="Grant Museum of Zoology">Grant Museum of Zoology</a> and the affiliated <a href="/wiki/University_College_Hospital" title="University College Hospital">University College Hospital</a>. Close by in Bloomsbury are the UCL Cancer Institute, the <a href="/wiki/The_Bartlett" title="The Bartlett">UCL Faculty of the Built Environment (The Bartlett)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Faculty_of_Laws" title="UCL Faculty of Laws">UCL Faculty of Laws</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Archaeology" title="UCL Institute of Archaeology">UCL Institute of Archaeology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Education" title="UCL Institute of Education">UCL Institute of Education</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Pharmacy" title="UCL School of Pharmacy">UCL School of Pharmacy</a>, the UCL School of Public Policy and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The area around <a href="/wiki/Queen_Square,_London" title="Queen Square, London">Queen Square</a> in Bloomsbury, close by to the main campus, is a hub for brain-related research and healthcare, with the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Cognitive_Neuroscience" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Institute of Cognitive Neuroscience">UCL Institute of Cognitive Neuroscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Neurology" title="UCL Institute of Neurology">UCL Institute of Neurology</a> located in the area along with the affiliated <a href="/wiki/National_Hospital_for_Neurology_and_Neurosurgery" title="National Hospital for Neurology and Neurosurgery">National Hospital for Neurology and Neurosurgery</a>. The <a href="/wiki/UCL_Great_Ormond_Street_Institute_of_Child_Health" title="UCL Great Ormond Street Institute of Child Health">UCL Great Ormond Street Institute of Child Health</a> and the affiliated <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital_for_Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children">Great Ormond Street Hospital for Children</a> are located adjacently, forming a hub for paediatric research and healthcare. The <a href="/wiki/UCL_Ear_Institute" title="UCL Ear Institute">UCL Ear Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Eastman_Dental_Institute" title="UCL Eastman Dental Institute">UCL Eastman Dental Institute</a> and the affiliated <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Throat,_Nose_and_Ear_Hospital" title="Royal National Throat, Nose and Ear Hospital">Royal National Throat, Nose and Ear Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Dental_Hospital" title="Eastman Dental Hospital">Eastman Dental Hospital</a> are located nearby in east Bloomsbury along <a href="/wiki/Gray%27s_Inn_Road" title="Gray&#39;s Inn Road">Gray's Inn Road</a> and form a hub for research and healthcare in audiology and dentistry respectively.
</p><p>Notable UCL buildings in Bloomsbury include the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Main_Building" title="UCL Main Building">UCL Main Building</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/(Octagon)-" class="mw-redirect" title="(Octagon)-">Octagon</a>, Quad, Cloisters and the Wilkins building designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Wilkins_(architect)" title="William Wilkins (architect)">William Wilkins</a>; the Cruciform Building, Gower Street (a red, cross-shaped building previously home to University College Hospital); and the Rockefeller Building, University Street, home to the original University College Hospital Medical School and named after the American oil magnate <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a> after support from the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller Foundation</a> in the 1920s. Due to its position within London and the historical nature of its buildings, including most notably the UCL Main Building and Quad, UCL has been used as a location for a number of film and television productions, including <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_in_the_House" title="Doctor in the House">Doctor in the House</a></i> (1954), <i><a href="/wiki/Gladiator_(2000_film)" title="Gladiator (2000 film)">Gladiator</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mummy_Returns" title="The Mummy Returns">The Mummy Returns</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> (2008) and <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> (2010).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of important institutions are based near to the main campus, including the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Medical_Association" title="British Medical Association">British Medical Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cancer_Research_UK" title="Cancer Research UK">Cancer Research UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gray%27s_Inn" title="Gray&#39;s Inn">Gray's Inn</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical Research Council (UK)">Medical Research Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/RADA" class="mw-redirect" title="RADA">RADA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Academy of Art">Royal Academy of Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institution" title="Royal Institution">Royal Institution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">Wellcome Trust</a>. Many University of London schools and institutes are also close by, including <a href="/wiki/Birkbeck,_University_of_London" title="Birkbeck, University of London">Birkbeck, University of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Business_School" title="London Business School">London Business School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Hygiene_%26_Tropical_Medicine" title="London School of Hygiene &amp; Tropical Medicine">London School of Hygiene &amp; Tropical Medicine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Veterinary_College" title="Royal Veterinary College">Royal Veterinary College</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Advanced_Study" title="School of Advanced Study">School of Advanced Study</a>, the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Oriental_and_African_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="School of Oriental and African Studies">School of Oriental and African Studies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senate_House_(University_of_London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate House (University of London)">Senate House Library</a>. The nearest <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> station is <a href="/wiki/Euston_Square_tube_station" title="Euston Square tube station">Euston Square</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Goodge_Street_tube_station" title="Goodge Street tube station">Goodge Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Square_tube_station" title="Russell Square tube station">Russell Square</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_Street_tube_station" title="Warren Street tube station">Warren Street</a> all nearby. The mainline railway stations at <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King's Cross</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras</a> are all within walking distance.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCL_East">UCL East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: UCL East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014 it was announced that UCL would be building an additional campus at the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Olympic_Park" title="Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park">Queen Elizabeth Olympic Park</a>, referred to as UCL East, as part of the development of the so-called <i>Olympicopolis</i> site at the southern edge of the park. UCL master planners were appointed in spring 2015, and the first University building was, at that time, estimated to be completed in time for academic year 2019/20.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was revealed in June 2016 that the UCL East expansion could see the university grow to 60,000 students. The proposed rate of growth was reported to be causing concern, with calls for it to be slowed down to ensure the university could meet financial stability targets.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Outline planning permission for UCL East was submitted in May 2017 by the <a href="/wiki/London_Legacy_Development_Corporation" title="London Legacy Development Corporation">London Legacy Development Corporation</a> and UCL, and granted in March 2018. Construction of the first phase of buildings is (as of March 2018)  expected to begin in 2019 with the first building (Pool Street West) expected to be completed for the start of the 2021 academic year and the second building (Marshgate 1) opening in phases from September 2022. As of March 2018, phase 1 is intended to have 50,000 m<sup>2</sup> of space, and to house 4,000 extra students and 260 extra academic staff, while the entire UCL East campus, when completed, is expected to have 180,000 m<sup>2</sup> of space, 40% of the size of UCL's central London campus.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The outline planning permission is for up to 190,800 m<sup>2</sup> of space with up to 160,060 m<sup>2</sup> of academic development and research space (including up to 16,000 m<sup>2</sup> of commercial research space), up to 50,880 m<sup>2</sup> of student accommodation, and up to 4,240 m<sup>2</sup> of retail space.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> According to the planning documents, construction of phase 2 (Pool Street East and Marshfield 2, 3 and 4) is expected to begin in 2030 and be completed by 2034, and the whole project will support 2,337 academic staff and 11,169 students.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The campus will include residences for up to 1,800 students.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> In June 2018, UCL revealed that the UK Government would be providing £100 million of funding for UCL East as part of its £151 million contribution to the £1.1 billion redevelopment of the Olympic Park as a cultural and education district to be known as the East Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 2018 UCL is offering degree courses at the Olympic Park, based at <i>UCL at Here East</i> at the northern end of the East Bank development.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_East_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_East-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sites">Other sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Elsewhere in Central London are the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Ophthalmology" title="UCL Institute of Ophthalmology">UCL Institute of Ophthalmology</a> (based in <a href="/wiki/Clerkenwell" title="Clerkenwell">Clerkenwell</a>), the Windeyer Institute (based in <a href="/wiki/Fitzrovia" title="Fitzrovia">Fitzrovia</a>), the UCL Institute of Orthopedics and Musculoskeletal Science (based in <a href="/wiki/Stanmore" title="Stanmore">Stanmore</a>), <a href="/wiki/Royal_Free_Hospital" title="Royal Free Hospital">The Royal Free Hospital</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Whittington_Hospital" title="Whittington Hospital">Whittington Hospital</a> campuses of the UCL Medical School, and a number of other teaching hospitals. The <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Management" title="UCL School of Management">UCL School of Management</a> is located at Level 38, <a href="/wiki/One_Canada_Square" title="One Canada Square">One Canada Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf" title="Canary Wharf">Canary Wharf</a>, London. The <a href="/wiki/Mullard_Space_Science_Laboratory" title="Mullard Space Science Laboratory">Department of Space and Climate Physics (Mullard Space Science Laboratory)</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Holmbury_St_Mary" title="Holmbury St Mary">Holmbury St Mary</a>, Surrey, and there is a UCL campus in Doha, Qatar specialised in archaeology, conservation and museum studies (to be transferred to <a href="/wiki/Hamad_Bin_Khalifa_University" title="Hamad Bin Khalifa University">Hamad Bin Khalifa University</a> in 2020 at the end of UCL's contact with the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation" title="Qatar Foundation">Qatar Foundation</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> From 2010 to 2015 UCL ran a University Preparatory Certificate course at Nazarbayev University in <a href="/wiki/Astana" title="Astana">Astana</a>, Kazakhstan,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and had a campus in Adelaide, Australia from 2010 to 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_and_administration">Organisation and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Organisation and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although UCL is a constituent college of the federal University of London, in most ways it is comparable with free-standing, self-governing and independently funded universities, and it awards its own degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL's governing body is the Council, which oversees the management and administration of UCL and the conduct of its affairs, subject to the advice of the Academic Board on matters of academic policy, and approves UCL's long-term plans.<sup id="cite_ref-governance_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> It delegates authority to the Provost, as chief executive, for the academic, corporate, financial, estate and human resources management of UCL. The Council normally meets six times each year. The Council comprises 20 members, of whom 11 are members external to UCL; seven are UCL academic staff, including the Provost, three UCL professors and three non-professorial staff; and two are UCL students. The Chair is appointed by Council for a term not normally exceeding five years. The Chair is <i>ex officio</i> Chair of the Honorary Degrees and Fellowships Committee, Nominations Committee and Remuneration and Strategy Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-governance_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The current Chair of the Council is Dame DeAnne Julius.
</p><p>UCL's principal academic and administrative officer is the President and Provost, who is also UCL's designated principal officer for the purposes of the Financial Memorandum with the Higher Education Funding Council for England (HEFCE).<sup id="cite_ref-governance_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The Provost is appointed by Council after consultation with the Academic Board, is responsible to the Council, and works closely with its members, and especially with the Chair of Council. The current and tenth Provost and President of UCL is <a href="/wiki/Michael_Arthur_(academic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Arthur (academic)">Michael Arthur</a>, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Grant" title="Malcolm Grant">Sir Malcolm Grant</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Vice-Provosts are appointed by the Provost, through the Council, to assist and advise the Provost as required. The Vice-Provosts are members of the Provost's Senior Management Team. There are presently six Vice-Provosts (for Education, Enterprise, Health, International, Research, and Operations).<sup id="cite_ref-governance_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Deans of UCL's faculties are appointed by Council and, together with the Vice-Provosts and the Director of Finance and Business Affairs, form the members of the Provost's Senior Management Team. The Deans' principal duties include advising the Provost and Vice-Provosts on academic strategy, staffing matters and resources for academic departments within their faculty; overseeing curricula and programme management at faculty level; liaising with Faculty Tutors on undergraduate admissions and student academic matters; overseeing examination matters at faculty level; and co-ordinating faculty views on matters relating to education and information support.<sup id="cite_ref-governance_125-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Provosts">List of Provosts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: List of Provosts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gregory_Foster" title="Gregory Foster">Sir Gregory Foster</a> (1906–1929)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Allen_Mawer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Allen Mawer (page does not exist)">Sir Allen Mawer</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q15983950#sitelinks-wikipedia" class="extiw" title="d:Q15983950"><span title="&quot;Allen Mawer&quot; in other languages">Wikidata</span></a>; <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/reasonator/?q=Q15983950">Reasonator</a>)</span> (1930–1942)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Randall_Pye" title="David Randall Pye">David Pye</a> (1943–1951)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ifor_Evans,_Baron_Evans_of_Hungershall" title="Ifor Evans, Baron Evans of Hungershall">Sir Ifor Evans</a> (1951–1966)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Noel_Annan,_Baron_Annan" title="Noel Annan, Baron Annan">Lord Annan</a> (1966–1978)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Lighthill" title="James Lighthill">Sir James Lighthill</a> (1979–1989)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Derek_Roberts" title="Derek Roberts">Sir Derek Roberts</a> (1989–1999;<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> 2002–2003)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Llewellyn_Smith" title="Christopher Llewellyn Smith">Sir Christopher Llewellyn Smith</a> (1999–2002)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Grant" title="Malcolm Grant">Sir Malcolm Grant</a> (2003–2013)<sup id="cite_ref-Former_Provosts_45-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Former_Provosts-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Arthur_(physician)" title="Michael Arthur (physician)">Michael Arthur</a> (2013–present)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_departments">Faculties and departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Faculties and departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Drayton_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UCL_Drayton_House.jpg/220px-UCL_Drayton_House.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UCL_Drayton_House.jpg/330px-UCL_Drayton_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/UCL_Drayton_House.jpg/440px-UCL_Drayton_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2815" data-file-height="1837" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Drayton_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drayton House, which houses the Faculty of Economics</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG/220px-UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG/330px-UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG/440px-UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1880" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_School_of_Pharmacy.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UCL School of Pharmacy building</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ucl_engineering.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ucl_engineering.jpg/220px-Ucl_engineering.jpg" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Ucl_engineering.jpg/330px-Ucl_engineering.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Ucl_engineering.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="303" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ucl_engineering.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Faculty of Engineering Sciences building</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg/220px-UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg/330px-UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg/440px-UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Bedford_Way.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bedford Way building, home to the UCL Institute of Education and the Departments of Geography, Psychology and Language</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Departments_of_University_College_London" title="Category:Departments of University College London">Category:Departments of University College London</a></div>
<p>UCL's research and teaching is organised within a network of faculties and academic departments. Faculties and academic departments are formally established by the UCL Council, the governing body of UCL, on the advice of the Academic Board, which is UCL's senior academic authority. UCL is a comprehensive university with teaching and research across the full range of the arts, humanities, social sciences, physical, biological and medical sciences, engineering and the built environment, although it does not currently have a veterinary, music, drama or nursing school.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> UCL is currently organised into the following 11 constituent faculties:<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
