<p>To facilitate greater interdisciplinary interaction in research and teaching UCL also has three strategic faculty groupings:
</p>
<ul><li>the UCL School of Life and Medical Sciences (comprising the Faculties of Brain Sciences, Life Sciences, Medical Sciences and Population Health Sciences);</li>
<li>the UCL School of the Built Environment, Engineering and Mathematical and Physical Sciences (comprising the UCL Faculty of the Built Environment, UCL Faculty of Engineering Sciences and UCL Faculty of Mathematical &amp; Physical Sciences);</li>
<li>the UCL Faculty of Arts &amp; Humanities, UCL Faculty of Laws, UCL Faculty of Social &amp; Historical Sciences and the UCL School of Slavonic &amp; East European Studies.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the financial year ended 31 July 2016, UCL had a total income (excluding share of joint ventures) of £1.36&#160;billion (2014/15 – £1.26&#160;billion) and a total expenditure of £1.23&#160;billion (2014/15 – £1.22&#160;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Key sources of income included £530.4&#160;million from research grants and contracts (2014/15 – £427.3&#160;million), £421.1&#160;million from tuition fees and education contracts (2014/15 – £364.2&#160;million), £192.1&#160;million from funding body grants (2014/15 – £195.2&#160;million) and £25.1&#160;million from donations and endowments (2014/15 – £20.3&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> During the 2015/16 financial year UCL had a capital expenditure of £146.6&#160;million (2014/15 – £149.3&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> At year end UCL had endowments of £100.9&#160;million (31 July 2015 – £104.1&#160;million) and total net assets of £1.19&#160;billion (31 July 2015 – £1.07&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014/15, UCL had the third-highest total income of any British university (after the University of Cambridge and the University of Oxford), and the third-highest income from research grants and contracts (after the University of Oxford and Imperial College London).<sup id="cite_ref-thefindat_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thefindat-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> For the 2015/16 academic year, UCL was allocated a total of £171.37 million for teaching and research from the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Funding_Council_for_England" title="Higher Education Funding Council for England">Higher Education Funding Council for England</a> (HEFCE), the highest amount allocated to any English university, of which £39.76 million is for teaching and £131.61 million is for research.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> According to a survey published by the Sutton Trust, UCL had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_UK_universities_by_endowment" title="List of UK universities by endowment">eighth-largest endowment of any British university</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL launched a 10-year, £300 million fundraising appeal in October 2004, at the time the largest appeal target set by a university in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> UCL launched a new £600 million fundraising campaign in September 2016 titled <i>"It's All Academic – The Campaign for UCL"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016, UCL signed a £280 million 30-year loan with the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a>, the largest loan ever borrowed by a UK university and largest ever loan by the EIB to a university.<sup id="cite_ref-FT28416_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT28416-137">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eibloan_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eibloan-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The monies are to be used to fund a £1.25 billion capital expenditure programme in Bloomsbury and Stratford.<sup id="cite_ref-FT28416_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT28416-137">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eibloan_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eibloan-138">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Some UCL academics oppose the expansion plans.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terms">Terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Terms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The UCL academic year is divided into three terms.<sup id="cite_ref-terms_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terms-140">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> For most departments except the Medical School, Term One runs from late September to mid December, Term Two from mid January to late March, and Term Three from late April to mid June.<sup id="cite_ref-terms_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terms-140">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Certain departments operate reading weeks in early November and mid February.<sup id="cite_ref-terms_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terms-140">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Logo.2C_arms_and_colours"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo,_arms_and_colours">Logo, arms and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Logo, arms and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Whereas most universities primarily use their logo on mundane documents but their coat of arms on official documents such as degree certificates, UCL exclusively uses its logo. The present logo was adopted as part of a rebranding exercise in August 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Baty_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baty-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Prior to that date, a different logo was used, in which the letters UCL were incorporated into a stylised representation of the Wilkins Building <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">portico</a>.
</p><p>UCL formerly made some use of a pseudo-heraldic "coat of arms" depicting a raised bent arm dressed in armour holding a green upturned open wreath.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> A version of this badge (not on a shield) appears to have been used by <a href="/wiki/University_College_London_Union" title="University College London Union">UCL Union</a> from shortly after its foundation in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> However, the arms have never been the subject of an official <a href="/wiki/Grant_of_arms" title="Grant of arms">grant of arms</a>, and depart from several of the rules and conventions of <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldry</a>. They are no longer formally used by the college, although they are still occasionally seen in unofficial contexts, or used in modified form by sports teams and societies. The <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazon</a> of the arms might be rendered as: <i>Purpure, on a wreath of the colours Argent and Blue Celeste, an arm in armour embowed Argent holding an upturned wreath of laurel Vert, beneath which two branches of laurel Or crossed at the nombril and bound with a bowed cord Or, beneath the nombril a motto of Blue Celeste upon which Cuncti adsint meritaeque expectent praemia palmae.</i> The motto is a quotation from <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i>, and translates into English as "Let all come who by merit deserve the most reward".<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL's traditional sporting and academic colours of purple and light blue are derived from the arms.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secularism">Secularism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Secularism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From its foundation the college was deliberately secular; the initial justification for this was that it would enable students of different Christian traditions (specifically <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>) to study alongside each other without conflict. UCL has retained this strict secular position and, unlike most other UK universities, has no specific religious prayer rooms. There has, however, been a Christian chaplaincy since 2005 and there is no restriction on religious groups among students. A "quiet contemplation room" also allows prayer for staff and students of all faiths.
</p>
<h3><span id="Memberships.2C_affiliations_and_partnerships"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Memberships,_affiliations_and_partnerships">Memberships, affiliations and partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Memberships, affiliations and partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg/220px-University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg/330px-University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg/440px-University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1171" data-file-height="722" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_Hospital_-_New_Building_-_London_-_020504.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main building of <a href="/wiki/University_College_Hospital" title="University College Hospital">University College Hospital</a></div></div></div>
<p>UCL is a constituent college of the federal University of London, of which it was one of the two founding members in 1836 (the other being <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King's College London</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>, an association of 24 British research universities established in 1994,<sup id="cite_ref-the91106_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the91106-145">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and of the <a href="/wiki/G5_(universities)" title="G5 (universities)">G5</a> lobbying group, which it established in early 2004 with the universities of Cambridge and Oxford, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-THE1_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE1-146">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> UCL is regarded as forming part of the ‘<a href="/wiki/Golden_triangle_(universities)" title="Golden triangle (universities)">golden triangle</a>’, an unofficial term for a set of leading universities located in the southern English cities of Cambridge, London and Oxford<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> including the universities of Cambridge and Oxford, Imperial College London, King's College London and the London School of Economics.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_European_Research_Universities" title="League of European Research Universities">League of European Research Universities</a> since January 2006. It is currently one of five British members (the others being the universities of Cambridge, Edinburgh and Oxford and Imperial College London).<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Other international groupings that UCL is a member of include the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Commonwealth_Universities" title="Association of Commonwealth Universities">Association of Commonwealth Universities</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_University_Association" title="European University Association">European University Association</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Universities_Research_Association" title="Universities Research Association">Universities Research Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> UCL has a major collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yale_UCL_Collaborative&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yale UCL Collaborative (page does not exist)">Yale UCL Collaborative</a>, and has hundreds of other research and teaching partnerships, including around 150 research links and 130 student-exchange partnerships with European universities.<sup id="cite_ref-fulbright.co.uk_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fulbright.co.uk-153">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/SES_(universities)" title="SES (universities)">SES</a> engineering and physical sciences research alliance since May 2013, which it formed with the universities of Cambridge, Oxford and Southampton and Imperial College London (King's College London subsequently joined in 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> UCL is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Young_Centre" title="Thomas Young Centre">Thomas Young Centre</a>, an alliance of London research groups working on the theory and simulation of materials; the other members are Imperial College London, King's College London and Queen Mary University of London.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> UCL is one of the five founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing_Institute" title="Alan Turing Institute">Alan Turing Institute</a>, the UK's national institute for data sciences (together with the universities of Cambridge, Edinburgh, Oxford and Warwick).<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> It also operates the <a href="/wiki/London_Centre_for_Nanotechnology" title="London Centre for Nanotechnology">London Centre for Nanotechnology</a>, a multidisciplinary research centre in physical and biomedical nanotechnology, in partnership with Imperial College London.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Crick_Institute_building,_Oct_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg/220px-Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg/330px-Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg/440px-Francis_Crick_Institute_building%2C_Oct_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Francis_Crick_Institute_building,_Oct_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick_Institute" title="Francis Crick Institute">Francis Crick Institute</a> building</div></div></div>
<p>UCL has a close partnership with <a href="/wiki/University_College_London_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">University College London Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a>; the Trust's hospitals are teaching sites for the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Medical_School" title="UCL Medical School">UCL Medical School</a>, UCL and the Trust are joint partners in the <a href="/wiki/UCLH/UCL_Biomedical_Research_Centre" title="UCLH/UCL Biomedical Research Centre">UCLH/UCL Biomedical Research Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Centre_for_Sport_and_Exercise_Medicine" title="National Centre for Sport and Exercise Medicine">Institute of Sport, Exercise and Health</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and both are members of the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Partners">UCL Partners</a> <a href="/wiki/Academic_health_science_centre" title="Academic health science centre">academic health science centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_Service_Journal_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_Service_Journal-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> UCL is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick_Institute" title="Francis Crick Institute">Francis Crick Institute</a>, a major biomedical research centre in London which is a partnership between <a href="/wiki/Cancer_Research_UK" title="Cancer Research UK">Cancer Research UK</a>, Imperial College London, King's College London, the <a href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(United_Kingdom)" title="Medical Research Council (United Kingdom)">Medical Research Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">Wellcome Trust</a> and UCL.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> UCL also operates the Bloomsbury Research Institute, a research institute focused on basic to clinical and population studies in bacteriology, parasitology and virology, in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Hygiene_%26_Tropical_Medicine" title="London School of Hygiene &amp; Tropical Medicine">London School of Hygiene &amp; Tropical Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL offers joint degrees with numerous other universities and institutions, including <a href="/wiki/Anna_Freud_Centre" title="Anna Freud Centre">The Anna Freud National Centre for Children and Families</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hong_Kong" title="University of Hong Kong">University of Hong Kong</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Imperial College London,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL is the sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Academy" title="UCL Academy">UCL Academy</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a> in the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">London Borough of Camden</a>. The school opened in September 2012 and was the first in the UK to have a university as sole sponsor.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> UCL also has a strategic partnership with <a href="/wiki/Newham_Collegiate_Sixth_Form_Centre" title="Newham Collegiate Sixth Form Centre">Newham Collegiate Sixth Form Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL is a founding member of Knowledge Quarter, a partnership of academic, cultural, research, scientific and media organisations based in the knowledge cluster in the Bloomsbury and King's Cross area of London.<sup id="cite_ref-guard41214_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard41214-172">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Other members of the partnership include the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and the Wellcome Trust.<sup id="cite_ref-guard41214_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard41214-172">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_staff">Faculty and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Faculty and staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2014/15 academic year, UCL had an average of 7,070 academic and research staff, the highest number of any UK university, of whom 5,360 were full-time and 1,710 part-time.<sup id="cite_ref-HESAstaff_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HESAstaff-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> UCL has 840 professors, the largest number of any British university.<sup id="cite_ref-factsandfigures_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsandfigures-173">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> As of August 2016 there were 56 Fellows of the Royal Society, 51 Fellows of the British Academy, 15 Fellows of the Royal Academy of Engineering and 121 Fellows of the Academy of Medical Sciences amongst UCL academic and research staff.<sup id="cite_ref-factsandfigures_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsandfigures-173">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_O%27Keefe_(neuroscientist)_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg/220px-John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg/330px-John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg/440px-John_O%27Keefe_%28neuroscientist%29_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1896" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_O%27Keefe_(neuroscientist)_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_O%27Keefe_(neuroscientist)" title="John O&#39;Keefe (neuroscientist)">John O'Keefe</a>, neuroscientist and the latest (2014) UCL faculty member to win a Nobel Prize (in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a> for his discovery of <a href="/wiki/Place_cell" title="Place cell">place cells</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>UCL has made cross-disciplinary research a priority and orientates its research around four "Grand Challenges", Global Health, Sustainable Cities, Intercultural Interaction and Human Wellbeing.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014/15, UCL had a total research income of £427.5 million, the third-highest of any British university (after the University of Oxford and Imperial College London).<sup id="cite_ref-thefindat_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thefindat-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Key sources of research income in that year were BIS research councils (£148.3 million), UK-based charities (£106.5 million), UK central government, local/health authorities and hospitals (£61.5 million), EU government bodies (£45.5 million), and UK industry, commerce and public corporations (£16.2 million).<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In 2015/16, UCL was awarded a total of £85.8 million in grants by <a href="/wiki/Research_Councils_UK" title="Research Councils UK">UK research councils</a>, the second-largest amount of any British university (after the University of Oxford), having achieved a 28% success rate.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> For the period to June 2015, UCL was the fifth-largest recipient of <a href="/wiki/Horizon_2020" class="mw-redirect" title="Horizon 2020">Horizon 2020</a> EU research funding, and the largest recipient of any university, with €49.93 million of grants received.<sup id="cite_ref-horizon2020_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horizon2020-176">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> UCL also had the fifth-largest number of projects funded of any organisation, with 94.<sup id="cite_ref-horizon2020_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-horizon2020-176">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a ranking of universities produced by SCImago Research Group, UCL is ranked 12th in the world (and 1st in Europe) in terms of total research output.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> According to data released in July 2008 by <a href="/wiki/ISI_Web_of_Knowledge" class="mw-redirect" title="ISI Web of Knowledge">ISI Web of Knowledge</a>, UCL is the 13th most-cited university in the world (and most-cited in Europe). The analysis covered citations from 1 January 1998 to 30 April 2008, during which 46,166 UCL research papers attracted 803,566 citations. The report covered citations in 21 subject areas and the results revealed some of UCL's key strengths, including: Clinical Medicine (1st outside North America); Immunology (2nd in Europe); Neuroscience &amp; Behaviour (1st outside North America and 2nd in the world); Pharmacology &amp; Toxicology (1st outside North America and 4th in the world); Psychiatry &amp; Psychology (2nd outside North America); and Social Sciences, General (1st outside North America).<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL submitted a total of 2,566 staff across 36 units of assessment to the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a> (REF) assessment, in each case the highest number of any UK university (compared with 1,793 UCL staff submitted to the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercise</a> (RAE 2008)).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-therae_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-therae-180">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In the REF results 43% of UCL's submitted research was classified as 4* (world-leading), 39% as 3* (internationally excellent), 15% as 2* (recognised internationally) and 2% as 1* (recognised nationally), giving an overall GPA of 3.22 (RAE 2008: 4* – 27%, 3* – 39%, 2* – 27% and 1* – 6%).<sup id="cite_ref-therae_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-therae-180">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-REFranking_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFranking-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In rankings produced by <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> based upon the REF results, UCL was ranked 1st overall for "research power" and joint 8th for GPA (compared to 4th and 7th respectively in equivalent rankings for the RAE 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-REFranking_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REFranking-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicine">Medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Medicine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Gower_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UCL_Gower_Street.jpg/220px-UCL_Gower_Street.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UCL_Gower_Street.jpg/330px-UCL_Gower_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/UCL_Gower_Street.jpg/440px-UCL_Gower_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Gower_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Cruciform Building on <a href="/wiki/Gower_Street_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gower Street (London)">Gower Street</a> houses the preclinical facilities of the UCL Medical School</div></div></div>
<p>UCL has offered courses in medicine since 1834, but the current <a href="/wiki/UCL_Medical_School" title="UCL Medical School">UCL Medical School</a> developed from mergers with the medical schools of the <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_Hospital" title="Middlesex Hospital">Middlesex Hospital</a> (founded in 1746) and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Free_Hospital" title="Royal Free Hospital">the Royal Free Hospital</a> (founded as the <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Medicine_for_Women" title="London School of Medicine for Women">London School of Medicine for Women</a> in 1874).<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Clinical medicine is primarily taught at the Royal Free Hospital, <a href="/wiki/University_College_Hospital" title="University College Hospital">University College Hospital</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Whittington_Hospital" title="Whittington Hospital">Whittington Hospital</a>, with other associated teaching hospitals including the <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Dental_Hospital" title="Eastman Dental Hospital">Eastman Dental Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital">Great Ormond Street Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moorfields_Eye_Hospital" title="Moorfields Eye Hospital">Moorfields Eye Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hospital_for_Neurology_and_Neurosurgery" title="National Hospital for Neurology and Neurosurgery">National Hospital for Neurology and Neurosurgery</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Throat,_Nose_and_Ear_Hospital" title="Royal National Throat, Nose and Ear Hospital">Royal National Throat, Nose and Ear Hospital</a>.
</p><p>UCL is a major centre for biomedical research. In a bibliometric analysis of biomedical and health research in England for the period 2004–13, UCL was found to have produced by far the highest number of highly cited publications of any institution, with 12,672 (compared to second-placed Oxford University with 9,952).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> UCL is part of three of the 20 biomedical research centres established by the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">NHS</a> in England – the <a href="/wiki/UCLH/UCL_Biomedical_Research_Centre" title="UCLH/UCL Biomedical Research Centre">UCLH/UCL Biomedical Research Centre</a>, the NIHR Biomedical Research Centre at Moorfields Eye Hospital NHS Foundation Trust and UCL Institute of Ophthalmology, and the NIHR Great Ormond Street Biomedical Research Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-nihr_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nihr-185">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In the latest round of <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health">Department of Health</a> funding for the 5 years from April 2017, the three UCL-affiliated biomedical research centres secured £168.6 million of the £811 million total funding nationwide, the largest amount awarded to any university and significantly higher than second-placed Oxford University (with £126.5 million).<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/UCL_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="UCL Partners">UCL Partners</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Academic_health_science_centre" title="Academic health science centre">academic health science centre</a> in Europe with a turnover of approximately £2&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Carvel_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carvel-187">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> UCL is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick_Institute" title="Francis Crick Institute">Francis Crick Institute</a> based next to <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras railway station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> It is one of the world's largest medical research centres, housing 1,250 scientists, and the largest of its kind in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-pr5_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pr5-189">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td><b><a href="/wiki/UCAS_Tariff" title="UCAS Tariff">Average Entry Tariff</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2019_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2019-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;note 5&#93;</a></sup>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bentham_House,_UCL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg/220px-Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg/330px-Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg/440px-Bentham_House%2C_UCL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2680" data-file-height="1886" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bentham_House,_UCL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bentham House, the main building of the UCL Faculty of Laws</div></div></div>
<p>Admission to UCL is highly selective with an average entry tariff for 2016–17 of 191 <a href="/wiki/UCAS_points" class="mw-redirect" title="UCAS points">UCAS points</a> (approximately equivalent to A*AAB or AAAA at <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level_(United_Kingdom)" title="GCE Advanced Level (United Kingdom)">A-level</a>), the 9th highest in the country and 3rd in London.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> UCL was one of the first universities in the UK to make use of the A* grade at A-Level (introduced in 2010) for admissions to courses including Economics, European Social and Political Studies, Law, Mathematics, Medicine, Theoretical Physics and Psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
The university gave offers of admission to 62.9% of its applicants in 2017, and had the 6th lowest offer rate in the <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> For 2017 entry, the university was one of only a few mainstream universities (along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">LSE</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">Warwick</a>) to have no courses available in <a href="/wiki/UCAS#Confirmation_and_Clearing" title="UCAS">Clearing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Clearing2017_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clearing2017-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Of UCL's undergraduates, 32.4% are <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Independent school (United Kingdom)">privately educated</a>, the eighth highest proportion amongst mainstream British universities.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> In the 2016-17 academic year, the university had a domicile breakdown of 59:12:30 of UK:EU:non-EU students respectively with a female to male ratio of 58:42.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Undergraduate law applicants are required to take the <a href="/wiki/National_Admissions_Test_for_Law" title="National Admissions Test for Law">National Admissions Test for Law</a><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> and undergraduate medical applicants are required to take the <a href="/wiki/BioMedical_Admissions_Test" title="BioMedical Admissions Test">BioMedical Admissions Test</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Applicants for European Social and Political Studies are required to take the <a href="/wiki/Thinking_Skills_Assessment" title="Thinking Skills Assessment">Thinking Skills Assessment</a> (TSA) should they be selected for an assessment day.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Some UCL departments interview undergraduate applicants prior to making an offer of admission.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Undergraduate subjects with the highest applicants to places ratio at UCL in 2015 included Architecture BSc (14:1 ratio),<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Economics BSc (Econ) (11:1 ratio),<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Engineering (Mechanical with Business Finance) MEng (10:1 ratio),<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> English BA (10:1 ratio),<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Fine Art BA (23:1 ratio),<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Law LL.B (16:1 ratio)<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> and Philosophy, Politics and Economics BSc (30:1 ratio).<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_programmes">Foundation programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Foundation programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL runs intensive one-year foundation courses that lead to a variety of degree programmes at UCL and other top UK universities. Called the <a href="/wiki/UCL_University_Preparatory_Certificate_(UPC)" title="UCL University Preparatory Certificate (UPC)">UCL University Preparatory Certificate</a>, the courses are targeted at international students of high academic potential whose education systems in their own countries usually do not offer qualifications suitable for direct admission. There are two pathways – one in science and engineering called the UPCSE; and one in the humanities called UPCH. The same courses run at the Centre for Preparatory Studies at <a href="/wiki/Nazarbayev_University" title="Nazarbayev University">Nazarbayev University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>. Students completing this course progress onto undergraduate programmes at Nazarbayev University.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Donaldson_Reading_Room,_UCL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg/220px-Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg/330px-Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg/440px-Donaldson_Reading_Room%2C_UCL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Donaldson_Reading_Room,_UCL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Donaldson Reading Room, part of UCL's Main Library</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG/220px-IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG/330px-IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG/440px-IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4080" data-file-height="2720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IOE_Newsam_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UCL Institute of Education's Newsam Library, the largest education library in Europe</div></div></div>
<p>The UCL library system comprises 17 libraries located across several sites within the main UCL campus and across <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury" title="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</a>, linked together by a central networking catalogue and request system called Explore.<sup id="cite_ref-libsites_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libsites-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The libraries contain a total of over 2 million books.<sup id="cite_ref-hefcelib_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hefcelib-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The largest library is the UCL Main Library, which is located in the UCL Main Building and contains collections relating to the arts and humanities, economics, history, law and public policy.<sup id="cite_ref-libsites_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libsites-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The second largest library is the UCL Science Library, which is located in the DMS Watson Building on Malet Place and contains collections relating to anthropology, engineering, geography, life sciences, management and the mathematical and physical sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-libsites_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libsites-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Other libraries include the <a href="/wiki/The_Bartlett" title="The Bartlett">UCL Bartlett</a> Library (architecture and town planning), the Cruciform Library (general clinical and medical sciences), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Eastman_Dental_Institute#Library" title="UCL Eastman Dental Institute">UCL Eastman Dental Institute Library</a> (oral health sciences), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Archaeology" title="UCL Institute of Archaeology">UCL Institute of Archaeology</a> Library (archaeology and egyptology), the UCL Institute of Education's <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Education#Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Education">Newsam Library</a> (education and related areas of social science), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Neurology#Library" title="UCL Institute of Neurology">UCL Institute of Neurology Rockefeller Medical Library</a> (neurosurgery and neuroscience), the <a href="/wiki/UCL_Institute_of_Ophthalmology#Library" title="UCL Institute of Ophthalmology">Joint Moorfields Eye Hospital &amp; the UCL Institute of Ophthalmology Library</a> (biomedicine, medicine, nursing, ophthalmology and visual science), the UCL Language &amp; Speech Science Library (audiology, communication disorders, linguistics &amp; phonetics, special education, speech &amp; language therapy and voice) and the <a href="/wiki/UCL_School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies#Library" title="UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies">UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies Library</a> (the economics, geography, history, languages, literature and politics of Eastern Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-libsites_213-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libsites-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL staff and students have full access to the main libraries of the University of London—the <a href="/wiki/Senate_House_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate House Library">Senate House Library</a> and the libraries of the Institutes of the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Advanced_Study" title="School of Advanced Study">School of Advanced Study</a>—which are located close to the main UCL campus in Bloomsbury.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> These libraries contain over 3.7&#160;million books and focus on the arts, humanities and social sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-hefcelib_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hefcelib-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>, which contains around 14 million books, is also located close to the main UCL campus and all UCL students and staff can apply for reference access.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2004, UCL Library Services has been collecting the scholarly work of UCL researchers to make it freely available on the internet via an <a href="/wiki/Institutional_repository" title="Institutional repository">open access repository</a> known as UCL Eprints.<sup id="cite_ref-eprints_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eprints-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The intention is that material curated by UCL Eprints will remain accessible indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-eprints_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eprints-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_collections">Museums and collections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Museums and collections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL's Special Collections contains UCL's collection of historical or culturally significant works. It is one of the foremost university collections of <a href="/wiki/Manuscripts" class="mw-redirect" title="Manuscripts">manuscripts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archives" class="mw-redirect" title="Archives">archives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rare_book" class="mw-redirect" title="Rare book">rare books</a> in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> It includes collections of <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> manuscripts and early printed books, as well as significant holdings of 18th-century works, and highly important 19th- and 20th-century collections of personal papers, archival material, and literature, covering a vast range of subject areas. Archives include the Latin American archives, the Jewish collections and the <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a> Archive.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Collections are often displayed in a series of glass cabinets in the Cloisters of the UCL Main Building.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL's most significant works are housed in the Strong Rooms. The special collection includes first editions of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Philosophiae_Naturalis_Principia_Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Philosophiae Naturalis Principia Mathematica">Principia</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Origin_of_Species" title="On the Origin of Species">On the Origin of Species</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/James_Joyce" title="James Joyce">James Joyce</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Ulysses_(novel)" title="Ulysses (novel)">Ulysses</a></i>. The earliest book in the collection is <i>The crafte to lyve well and to dye well</i>, printed in 1505.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flaxman_Gallery,_UCL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/220px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/330px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/440px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flaxman_Gallery,_UCL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Flaxman Gallery</div></div></div>
<p>UCL is responsible for several museums and collections in a wide range of fields across the arts and sciences, including:<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Petrie_Museum_of_Egyptian_Archaeology" title="Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology">Petrie Museum of Egyptian Archaeology</a>: one of the leading collections of Egyptian and Sudanese archaeology in the world. Open to the public on a regular basis.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>UCL Art Museum: the art collections date from 1847, when a collection of sculpture models and drawings by the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">neoclassical</a> artist <a href="/wiki/John_Flaxman" title="John Flaxman">John Flaxman</a> was presented to UCL. There are over 10,000 pieces dating from the 15th century onwards including drawings by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Mallord_William_Turner" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Mallord William Turner">Turner</a>, etchings by <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt_Harmenszoon_van_Rijn" class="mw-redirect" title="Rembrandt Harmenszoon van Rijn">Rembrandt</a>, and works by many leading 20th century British artists. The works on paper are displayed in the Strang Print Room, which has limited regular opening times. The other works may be viewed by appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Flaxman Gallery: a series of plaster casts of full-size details of sculptures by John Flaxman is located inside the Main Library under the central dome of the UCL Main Building.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grant_Museum_of_Zoology_and_Comparative_Anatomy" title="Grant Museum of Zoology and Comparative Anatomy">Grant Museum of Zoology and Comparative Anatomy</a>: a diverse Natural History collection covering the whole of the animal kingdom. Includes rare <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quagga" title="Quagga">quagga</a> skeletons. A teaching and research collection, it is named after <a href="/wiki/Robert_Edmund_Grant" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Edmund Grant">Robert Edmund Grant</a>, UCL's first professor of comparative anatomy and zoology from 1828, now mainly noted for having tutored the undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Charles_Robert_Darwin" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Robert Darwin">Charles Robert Darwin</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> in the 1826–1827 session.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Geology Collections: founded around 1855. Primarily a teaching resource and may be visited by appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Archaeology_Collections" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Archaeology Collections">Institute of Archaeology Collections</a>: items include prehistoric ceramics and stone artefacts from many parts of the world, the Petrie collection of Palestinian artefacts, and Classical Greek and Roman ceramics. Visits by appointment only.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">Ethnography</a> Collections: this collection exemplifying Material Culture holds an enormous variety of objects, textiles and artefacts from all over the world. Visits by appointment only.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Galton Collection: the scientific instruments, papers and personal memorabilia of Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Galton" title="Francis Galton">Francis Galton</a>. Housed in the department of biology. Visits by appointment only.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Science Collections: diverse collections primarily accumulated in the course of UCL's own work, including the operating table on which the first anaesthetic was administered. Items may be a viewed by appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
