</th><td> 14</td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td colspan="3"><div style="text-align: center;"> <b><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">National rankings</a></b> </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Complete_University_Guide" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Complete</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Complete_League_Table_2019_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Complete_League_Table_2019-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 10</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Guardian" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">The Guardian</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Guardian_University_Guide_2019-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 11</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#The_Sunday_Times" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Times / Sunday Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2019_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Times_and_Sunday_Times_University_Guide_2019-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><br /></th>
<td> 8</td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td colspan="3"><div style="text-align: center;"> <b> British Government assessment </b> </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"> <i><a href="/wiki/Teaching_Excellence_Framework" title="Teaching Excellence Framework">Teaching Excellence Framework</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-TEF_2018_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TEF_2018-237">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</th><td> <i>Silver</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<dl><dt>International</dt></dl>
<p>In the 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>, UCL is ranked 16th in the world (and 3rd in Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2017_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_2017-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In the 2016 subject tables it was ranked 8th in the world (and 2nd in Europe) for Clinical Medicine &amp; Pharmacy,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> joint 51st to 75th in the world (and joint 10th in Europe) for Engineering, Technology and Computer Sciences,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> 9th in the world (and 2nd in Europe) for Life &amp; Agricultural Sciences,<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> joint 51st to 75th in the world (and joint 14th in Europe) for Natural Sciences and Mathematics<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> and joint 51st to 75th in the world (and joint 12th in Europe) for Social Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2018/19 <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>, UCL is ranked 10th in the world (and 5th in Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017/18 faculty rankings it is ranked joint 18th in the world (4th in Europe) for Arts and Humanities,<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> joint 53rd in the world (15th in Europe) for Engineering and Technology,<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> 11th in the world (4th in Europe) for Life Sciences and Medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> 62nd in the world (18th in Europe) for Natural Sciences,<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> and joint 30th in the world (6th in Europe) for Social Sciences and Management.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017/18 Rankings by Subject, UCL is ranked in 37 subjects, of which 35 are in the world top 100 and 16 are in the world top 20. It is ranked in the world top 10 for ten subjects: Anthropology (10th), Archaeology (3rd), Architecture (2nd), Anatomy &amp; Physiology (joint 4th), Dentistry (6th), Education and Training (1st), Geography (8th), Medicine (9th), Pharmacy &amp; Pharmacology (8th) and Psychology (joint 8th). In the QS Graduate Employability Ranking, UCL is ranked 24th.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2018 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>, UCL is ranked 16th in the world (and 5th in Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-THE_World_University_Rankings_2017-18_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_World_University_Rankings_2017-18-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In the 2016/17 subject tables it was ranked 4th in the world (and 2nd in Europe) for Arts and Humanities,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> 6th in the world (and 4th in Europe) for Clinical, Pre-Clinical and Health,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> 12th in the world (and 6th in Europe) for Computer Science,<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> joint 38th in the world (and 12th in Europe) for Engineering and Technology,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> 12th in the world (and 4th in Europe) for Life Sciences,<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> joint 23rd in the world (and 8th in Europe) for Physical Sciences<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> and 14th in the world (and 3rd in Europe) for Social Sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> In the 2017 <i>Times Higher Education World Reputation Rankings</i>, UCL is ranked 16th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-thereputat_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thereputat-257">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> In the 2015 <i>Times Higher Education Global Employability University Ranking</i>, UCL is ranked 48th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-theemployability_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theemployability-258">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL is ranked 16th in the world (2nd in Europe) for number of publications and 26th in the world (6th in Europe) for quality of publications in the 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">CWTS Leiden Ranking</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> UCL is ranked 10th in the world (2nd in Europe) in the 2017 <i>National Taiwan University Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> UCL is ranked 17th in the world (8th in Europe) in the 2017 <i><a href="/wiki/Round_University_Ranking" title="Round University Ranking">Round University Ranking</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> UCL is ranked 5th in the world (2nd in Europe) in the 2016/17 <i><a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> In the 2018 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report_Best_Global_University_Ranking" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report Best Global University Ranking">U.S. News &amp; World Report Best Global University Ranking</a></i>, UCL is ranked 22nd in the world (4th in Europe).<sup id="cite_ref-USNEWSRANKING_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNEWSRANKING-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>National</dt></dl>
<p>UCL is consistently one of the top 10 multi-faculty universities in <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">UK university rankings</a>, which place more emphasis on the undergraduate student experience than global rankings, using criteria such as teaching quality and learning resources, entry standards, employment prospects, research quality and dropout rates. In the 2018 <i>Times Higher Education</i> "Table of Tables", which is based on the combined results of the UK’s three main domestic university rankings, UCL is ranked joint 7th.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> 10-year (1998–2007) average ranking of British universities based on consistent league table performance, UCL was ranked 5th overall in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> UCL is one of only eight universities (along with the other members of the <a href="/wiki/G5_(universities)" title="G5 (universities)">G5</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bath" title="University of Bath">Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">Warwick</a>) to have never been outside the top 15 in one of the three main domestic rankings between 2008-2017.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>  For 2017 entry UCL, along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">LSE</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warwick" title="University of Warwick">Warwick</a> were one of the few mainstream institutions to opt out of Clearing.<sup id="cite_ref-Clearing2017_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clearing2017-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2019 <i>Complete University Guide</i> subject tables, UCL is ranked in the top 10 in 29 subjects, and is ranked second for Town &amp; Country Planning and Landscape Design and third for Building and Politics among others.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> In a 2015 <i>Times Higher Education</i> study UCL was chosen as the 8th best university in the UK for the quality of graduates according to recruiters from the UK's major companies.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_activities">Commercial activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Commercial activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>UCL has significant commercial activities and in 2014/15 these generated around £155 million in revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> UCL's principal commercial activities include <a href="/wiki/UCL_Business" title="UCL Business">UCL Business</a>, UCL Consultants, and catering and accommodation services.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> UCL also participates in a number of commercial joint ventures, including EuroTempest Ltd and Imanova Ltd.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCL_Business">UCL Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: UCL Business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/UCL_Business" title="UCL Business">UCL Business</a></div>
<p>UCL Business (UCLB) is a <a href="/wiki/Technology_transfer" title="Technology transfer">technology transfer</a> company which is wholly owned by UCL. It has three main activities: licensing technologies, creating spin-out companies, and project management.<sup id="cite_ref-uclbwwd_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclbwwd-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> UCLB supports spin-out companies in areas including discovery disclosure, commercialisation, business plan development, contractual advice, incubation support, recruitment of management teams and identification of investors.<sup id="cite_ref-uclbwwd_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclbwwd-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> In the area of licensing technoloiges, UCLB provides commercial, legal and administrative advice to help companies broker licensing agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-uclbwwd_269-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclbwwd-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> UCLB also provides UCL departments and institutes with project management services for single or multi-party collaborative industry projects.<sup id="cite_ref-uclbwwd_269-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclbwwd-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCLB had a turnover of £8 million in 2014/15 and as at 31 July 2015 had equity holdings in 61 companies.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCL_Consultants">UCL Consultants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: UCL Consultants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL Consultants (UCLC) is an academic consultancy services company which is wholly owned by UCL.<sup id="cite_ref-uclca_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclca-271">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> It provides four main service offerings: Academic Consultancy, Testing &amp; Analysis, Expert Witness, and Training &amp; Short Courses.<sup id="cite_ref-uclca_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclca-271">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> As at 31 July 2015 UCLC had around 1,100 registered consultants.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCLC had a turnover of £10.1 million in 2014/15.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCL_Press">UCL Press</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: UCL Press">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL Press is a university press wholly owned by UCL.<sup id="cite_ref-uclpr_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclpr-272">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> It was the first fully <a href="/wiki/Open_access" title="Open access">open access</a> university press in the UK, and publishes monographs, textbooks and other academic books in a wide range of academic areas which are available to download for free, in addition to a number of journals<sup id="cite_ref-uclpr2_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclpr2-273">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> As of May 2018, UCL Press had had more than 1 million downloads of its open access books.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imanova">Imanova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Imanova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Imanova is a joint venture company of UCL, Imperial College London, Kings College London and the Medical Research Council which owns and
manages the Clinical Imaging Centre located at Imperial College London’s <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Hospital" title="Hammersmith Hospital">Hammersmith Hospital</a> campus.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg/220px-UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg/330px-UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg/440px-UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2373" data-file-height="1685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_summer_ball_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Performers at the 2014 UCL summer ball</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2014/15 academic year UCL had a total of 35,615 students, of whom 16,830 were undergraduate and 18,785 were postgraduate.<sup id="cite_ref-hesa_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hesa-275">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> In that year, UCL had the <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_enrolment" title="List of universities in the United Kingdom by enrolment">third-largest total number of students of any university in the United Kingdom</a> (after the Open University and the University of Manchester), and the largest number of postgraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-hesa_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hesa-275">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013/14 87% of UCL's students were full-time and 13% part-time,<sup id="cite_ref-studenttablea_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studenttablea-276">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> and 54% were female and 46% male.<sup id="cite_ref-studenttablee_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studenttablee-277">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> In 2013/14, 12,330 UCL students were from outside the UK (43% of the total number of students in that year), of whom 5,504 were from Asia, 3,679 from the European Union ex. the United Kingdom, 1,195 from North America, 516 from the Middle East, 398 from Africa, 254 from Central and South America, and 166 from Australasia.<sup id="cite_ref-studenttablep_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-studenttablep-278">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 31 July 2015, UCL had around 220,000 alumni across 190 countries, of whom around 137,000 were based in the United Kingdom (and approximately 60,000 were based in London). The largest alumni communities outside of the UK are in the United States, Greece and China.<sup id="cite_ref-finstat_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finstat-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UCL_Union">UCL Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: UCL Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_London_Union.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/University_College_London_Union.jpg/170px-University_College_London_Union.jpg" width="170" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/University_College_London_Union.jpg/255px-University_College_London_Union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/University_College_London_Union.jpg/340px-University_College_London_Union.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1957" data-file-height="2990" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_College_London_Union.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main UCL Union building situated on Gordon Street</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_College_London_Union" title="University College London Union">University College London Union</a></div>
<p>Founded in 1893, the UCL Union is one of the oldest students' unions in England, although postdating the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Guild_of_Students" title="Liverpool Guild of Students">Liverpool Guild of Students</a> which formed a student representative council in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LGoS_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LGoS-279">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> UCL Union operates both as the representative voice for UCL students, and as a provider of a wide range of services. It is democratically controlled through General Meetings and referendums, and is run by elected student officers. The Union has provided a prominent platform for political campaigning of all kinds in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  It also supports a range of services, including numerous clubs and societies, sports facilities, an advice service, and a number of bars, cafes and shops.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> The union is also responsible for the organisation of a number of events, including, amongst others, the college's annual summer ball.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There are currently over 150 clubs and societies under the umbrella of the UCL Union, including: UCL Snowsports (one of the largest sports society at UCL, responsible for organising the annual UCL ski trip),<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Pi Media (responsible for <i><a href="/wiki/Pi_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Pi Magazine">Pi Magazine</a></i> and <i>Pi Newspaper</i>, UCL's official student publications);<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> UCL Union Debating Society, UCL's second oldest society (established 1829),<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> UCL Union Film Society, one of the country's oldest film societies with past members including Christopher Nolan;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cheese_Grater" title="The Cheese Grater">The Cheese Grater</a></i> (a student magazine containing a mix of news investigations and humorous items); and the University College London Investment Society, one of the largest and most popular career societies at UCL .<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2018)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL Union runs over 50 sports clubs, including UCL Cricket Club (Men's and Women's as well as Medical School clubs), UCL Boat Club (Men's and Women's clubs), UCL Cross Country and Athletics Club and UCL Rugby Club (Men's and Women's as well as Medical School clubs).<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL clubs compete in inter-university fixtures in the <a href="/wiki/British_Universities_and_Colleges_Sport" title="British Universities and Colleges Sport">British Universities and Colleges Sport</a> (BUCS) competition in a range of sports, including basketball, cricket, fencing, football, hockey, netball, rugby union and tennis. In the 2014/15 season, UCL finished in 24th position in the final BUCS rankings of 151 participating higher education institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>UCL sports facilities include a fitness centre at the main UCL campus in Bloomsbury, a sports centre in <a href="/wiki/Somers_Town,_London" title="Somers Town, London">Somers Town</a> and a 90-acre athletics ground in Shenley.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UCL mascot is Phineas Maclino, or Phineas, a wooden tobacconist's sign of a kilted Jacobite Highlander stolen from outside a shop in <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Court_Road" title="Tottenham Court Road">Tottenham Court Road</a> during the celebrations of the <a href="/wiki/Relief_of_Ladysmith" title="Relief of Ladysmith">relief of Ladysmith</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a>, in March 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> This establishment of mascots at both UCL and King's saw the beginning of mascotry, where Phineas would be kidnapped by King's and then this act would be revenged by UCL. In 1922, Phineas was briefly stolen by King's, and later during the 1927 rag the King's mascot 'Reggie the Lion' was captured by UCL students and his body filled with rotten apples. In 1993, the university's centenary year, Phineas was placed in the third floor bar of 25 Gordon Street and the bar named after him.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rivalry_with_King.27s_College_London"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_King's_College_London">Rivalry with King's College London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rivalry with King&#039;s College London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg/220px-UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg/330px-UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg/440px-UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL-KCL_Varsity_Rugby_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UCL's Tom Brocket attacks in his team's 2014 Varsity victory. UCL's traditional rivalry with King's College is nowadays most noticeable at the annual varsity rugby game</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London%E2%80%93UCL_rivalry" title="King&#39;s College London–UCL rivalry">King's College London–UCL rivalry</a></div>
<p>UCL has a long-running, mostly friendly rivalry with <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King's College London</a>, which has historically been known as "Rags".<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> UCL students have been referred to by students from King's as the "Godless Scum of Gower Street", in reference to a comment made at the founding of King's, which was based on Christian principles. UCL students in turn referred to King's as "Strand Polytechnic".
</p><p>The King's' mascot, <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London_Students%27_Union#Mascot" title="King&#39;s College London Students&#39; Union">Reggie the Lion</a>, went missing in the 1990s and was recovered after being found dumped in a field. It was restored at the cost of around £15,000 and then placed on display in the students' union.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> It is in a glass case and filled with concrete to prevent theft, particularly by UCL students who once castrated it. In turn, King's' students are also believed to have once stolen Phineas, a UCL mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> It is often claimed that King's' students played football with the embalmed head of <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bentham" title="Jeremy Bentham">Jeremy Bentham</a>. Although the head was indeed stolen, the football story is a myth or legend which is unsupported by official UCL documentation about Bentham available next to his display case (his auto-icon) in the UCL cloisters. The head is now kept in the UCL vaults.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_campaigns">Student campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Student campaigns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Student campaigns at UCL have included: UCLU Free Education Campaign (a campaign for the return of free and non-marketised higher education); the London Living wage Campaign (a campaign for a basic minimum wage for all UCL staff); Disarm UCL (a campaign which successfully persuaded UCL not to invest in defence companies); and Save UCL (this name has been used by two campaigns: one in 2006 which opposed a merger between UCL and Imperial College London in 2006, and a more recent one against education cuts).
</p><p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/2010_UK_student_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 UK student protests">protests against the UK Government's plans to increase student fees</a>, around 200 students occupied the Jeremy Bentham Room and part of the <a href="/wiki/Slade_School_of_Fine_Art" title="Slade School of Fine Art">Slade School of Fine Art</a> for over two weeks during November and December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-students_stage_day_of_protests_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-students_stage_day_of_protests-294">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uclprotest_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclprotest-295">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> The university successfully obtained a court order to evict the students but stated that it did not intend to enforce the order if possible.<sup id="cite_ref-uclprotest_295-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclprotest-295">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg/220px-UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg/330px-UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg/440px-UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UCL_Frances_Gardner_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frances Gardner House</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Halls_of_residence_at_University_College_London" title="Halls of residence at University College London">Halls of residence at University College London</a></div>
<p>All first-year undergraduate students and overseas first-year postgraduates at UCL are guaranteed university accommodation.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> The majority of second- and third-year undergraduate students and graduate students find their own accommodation in the private sector; graduate students may apply for accommodation but places are limited.
</p><p>UCL students are eligible to apply for places in the University of London intercollegiate halls of residence.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> The halls are: Canterbury Hall, Commonwealth Hall, College Hall, <a href="/wiki/Connaught_Hall,_London" title="Connaught Hall, London">Connaught Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hughes_Parry_Hall,_London" title="Hughes Parry Hall, London">Hughes Parry Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Hall,_London" title="International Hall, London">International Hall</a> near <a href="/wiki/Russell_Square" title="Russell Square">Russell Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury" title="Bloomsbury">Bloomsbury</a>; Lillian Penson Hall in <a href="/wiki/Paddington" title="Paddington">Paddington</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Nutford_House,_London" title="Nutford House, London">Nutford House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Marble_Arch" title="Marble Arch">Marble Arch</a>. Some students are also selected to live in <a href="/wiki/International_Students_House,_London" title="International Students House, London">International Students House</a>.
</p><p>In 2013, a new student accommodation building on <a href="/wiki/Caledonian_Road,_London" title="Caledonian Road, London">Caledonian Road</a> was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Carbuncle_Cup" title="Carbuncle Cup">Carbuncle Cup</a> and named the country's worst new building by <i><a href="/wiki/Building_Design" title="Building Design">Building Design</a></i> magazine, with the comment "this is a building that the jury struggled to see as remotely fit for human occupation". Islington Council had originally turned down planning permission for the building, but this had been overturned on appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_associated_with_University_College_London" title="List of people associated with University College London">List of people associated with University College London</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_University_College_London" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with University College London">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with University College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_College_London_people_in_the_Law" title="List of University College London people in the Law">List of University College London people in the Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/School_of_Slavonic_and_East_European_Studies#Notable_alumni_and_staff" class="mw-redirect" title="School of Slavonic and East European Studies">School of Slavonic and East European Studies §&#160;Notable alumni and staff</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slade_School_of_Fine_Art#Notable_alumni" title="Slade School of Fine Art">Slade School of Fine Art §&#160;Notable alumni</a></div>
<p>UCL alumni include <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> (leader of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">Indian independence movement</a>), <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a> (inventor of the telephone), <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Francis Crick</a> (co-discoverer of the structure of DNA), <a href="/wiki/William_Stanley_Jevons" title="William Stanley Jevons">William Stanley Jevons</a> (early pioneer of modern Economics), <a href="/wiki/Jomo_Kenyatta" title="Jomo Kenyatta">Jomo Kenyatta</a> ("Father of the Nation" of Kenya), <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a> (founder of Ghana and "Father of African Nationalism") and <a href="/wiki/Charles_K._Kao" title="Charles K. Kao">Charles K. Kao</a> ("Godfather of <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a>"). Notable former staff include <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk">Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk</a> ("Father of the Nation" of Czechoslovakia"), <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a> (proposer of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_mechanism" title="Higgs mechanism">Higgs mechanism</a> which predicted the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>), <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Freud" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucien Freud">Lucien Freud</a> (artist) and <a href="/wiki/William_Ramsay" title="William Ramsay">Sir William Ramsay</a> (discoverer of all of the naturally occurring noble gases).
</p><p>Nobel Prizes have been awarded to <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_University_College_London" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with University College London">at least 30 UCL academics and students</a> (17 of which were in Physiology &amp; Medicine), as well as three <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

		</div></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty_and_staff">Notable faculty and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable faculty and staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notable former UCL faculty and staff include <a href="/wiki/Jocelyn_Bell_Burnell" title="Jocelyn Bell Burnell">Jocelyn Bell Burnell</a> (co-discoverer of radio <a href="/wiki/Pulsars" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulsars">pulsars</a>), <a href="/wiki/A._S._Byatt" title="A. S. Byatt">A. S. Byatt</a> (writer), <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Dworkin" title="Ronald Dworkin">Ronald Dworkin</a> (legal philosopher and scholar of constitutional law),<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Austin_(legal_philosopher)" title="John Austin (legal philosopher)">John Austin</a> (legal philosopher, founder of <a href="/wiki/Legal_positivism" title="Legal positivism">analytical jurisprudence</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A.J._Ayer" class="mw-redirect" title="A.J. Ayer">Sir A.J. Ayer</a> (philosopher), <a href="/wiki/Sir_Ambrose_Fleming" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Ambrose Fleming">Sir Ambrose Fleming</a> (inventor of the first thermionic valve, the fundamental building block of electronics),<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lucian_Freud" title="Lucian Freud">Lucian Freud</a> (painter),<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_J_Goldberg" title="Andrew J Goldberg">Andrew J Goldberg OBE</a> (Chairman of Medical Futures),<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> (the proposer of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_mechanism" title="Higgs mechanism">Higgs mechanism</a>, which predicted the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a>), <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Huxley" title="Andrew Huxley">Andrew Huxley</a> (<a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">biophysicist</a>), <a href="/wiki/William_Stanley_Jevons" title="William Stanley Jevons">William Stanley Jevons</a> (economist), <a href="/wiki/Frank_Kermode" title="Frank Kermode">Sir Frank Kermode</a> (literary critic), <a href="/wiki/A._E._Housman" title="A. E. Housman">A. E. Housman</a> (classical scholar, and poet), <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk">Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk</a> (first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Czechoslovakia" title="List of Presidents of Czechoslovakia">President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and "Father of the Nation"), <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">John Stuart Mill</a> (philosopher), <a href="/wiki/Peter_T._Kirstein" title="Peter T. Kirstein">Peter Kirstein CBE</a> (computer scientist, significant role in the creation of the Internet), <a href="/wiki/George_R._Price" title="George R. Price">George R. Price</a> (<a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">population geneticist</a>), <a href="/wiki/Edward_Teller" title="Edward Teller">Edward Teller</a> ("Father of the <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_Bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen Bomb">Hydrogen Bomb</a>"), <a href="/wiki/David_Kemp_(physicist)" title="David Kemp (physicist)">David Kemp</a> (the first scientist to demonstrate the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Otoacoustic_emission" title="Otoacoustic emission">otoacoustic emissions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dadabhai_Naoroji" title="Dadabhai Naoroji">Dadabhai Naoroji</a> (Indian Parsi leader, the first Asian to be elected to UK House of Commons).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg/170px-William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg" width="170" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg/255px-William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg/340px-William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="776" data-file-height="818" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Bayliss_1918b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Bayliss" title="William Bayliss">William Bayliss</a>, co-discoverer of <a href="/wiki/Secretin" title="Secretin">Secretin</a>, the first identified hormone</div></div></div>
<p>All five of the naturally occurring <a href="/wiki/Noble_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Noble gases">noble gases</a> were discovered at UCL by Professor of Chemistry <a href="/wiki/William_Ramsay" title="William Ramsay">Sir William Ramsay</a>, after whom Ramsay Hall is named.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hormones were first discovered at UCL by <a href="/wiki/William_Bayliss" title="William Bayliss">William Bayliss</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Starling" title="Ernest Starling">Ernest Starling</a>, the former also an alumnus of UCL.<sup id="cite_ref-Tata_490–496_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tata_490–496-309">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notable UCL alumni include:
</p>
<ul><li><b>artists</b> including <a href="/wiki/William_Coldstream" title="William Coldstream">Sir William Coldstream</a> (realist painter), <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Lewis" title="Wyndham Lewis">Wyndham Lewis</a> (vorticist painter), <a href="/wiki/Antony_Gormley" title="Antony Gormley">Antony Gormley</a> (sculptor), <a href="/wiki/Augustus_John" title="Augustus John">Augustus John</a> (painter, draughtsman and etcher),<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Judah" title="Gerry Judah">Gerry Judah</a> (artist and designer), <a href="/wiki/Ben_Nicholson" title="Ben Nicholson">Ben Nicholson</a> (abstract painter), <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Paolozzi" title="Eduardo Paolozzi">Sir Eduardo Paolozzi</a> (sculptor and artist) and <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_el-Salahi" title="Ibrahim el-Salahi">Ibrahim el-Salahi</a> (artist painter and former diplomat);</li>
<li><b>authors</b> including <a href="/wiki/Edith_Clara_Batho" title="Edith Clara Batho">Edith Clara Batho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Briggs" title="Raymond Briggs">Raymond Briggs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Browning" title="Robert Browning">Robert Browning</a>, <a href="/wiki/G._K._Chesterton" title="G. K. Chesterton">G. K. Chesterton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tele20612_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele20612-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Crystal" title="David Crystal">David Crystal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stella_Gibbons" title="Stella Gibbons">Stella Gibbons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clive_Sansom" title="Clive Sansom">Clive Sansom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Knox_(author)" title="Tom Knox (author)">Sean Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marie_Stopes" title="Marie Stopes">Marie Stopes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-tele20612_312-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele20612-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helen_MacInnes" title="Helen MacInnes">Helen MacInnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore" title="Rabindranath Tagore">Rabindranath Tagore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_Vikelas" title="Demetrius Vikelas">Demetrius Vikelas</a> (who was also the first <a href="/wiki/Presidents_of_the_International_Olympic_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidents of the International Olympic Committee">President of the International Olympic Committee</a>);</li>
<li><b>business-oriented people</b> including <a href="/wiki/Colin_Chapman" title="Colin Chapman">Colin Chapman</a> (founder of <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Cars" title="Lotus Cars">Lotus Cars</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demis_Hassabis" title="Demis Hassabis">Demis Hassabis</a> (co-founder and CEO of <a href="/wiki/DeepMind" title="DeepMind">DeepMind</a>), <a href="/wiki/Lord_Digby_Jones" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Digby Jones">Lord Digby Jones</a> (former Director-General of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">Confederation of British Industry</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Waterhouse" title="Edwin Waterhouse">Edwin Waterhouse</a> (founding partner of the professional services firm <a href="/wiki/PwC" class="mw-redirect" title="PwC">PwC</a>) and billionaire Farhad Moshiri (Everton F.C part owner).<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>medical researchers, specialists &amp; scientists</b> including <a href="/wiki/Archie_Cochrane" title="Archie Cochrane">Archie Cochrane</a> (medic, researcher, and pioneer of evidence-based medicine),<sup id="cite_ref-Cochrane_Org_History_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cochrane_Org_History-316">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jane_Dacre" title="Jane Dacre">Jane Dacre</a> (current President of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Physicians" title="Royal College of Physicians">Royal College of Physicians</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Farrar" title="Jeremy Farrar">Jeremy Farrar</a> (current Director of the <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">Wellcome Trust</a>), <a href="/wiki/Clare_Gerada" title="Clare Gerada">Clare Gerada</a> (previous President of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_General_Practitioners" title="Royal College of General Practitioners">Royal College of General Practitioners</a>), <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lister,_1st_Baron_Lister" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Lister, 1st Baron Lister">Joseph Lister</a> (pioneer of antiseptic surgery) and <a href="/wiki/Clare_Marx" title="Clare Marx">Clare Marx</a> (current President of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons_of_England" title="Royal College of Surgeons of England">Royal College of Surgeons of England</a>); <a href="/wiki/Marc_Tessier-Lavigne" title="Marc Tessier-Lavigne">Marc Tessier-Lavigne</a> (current president of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>).</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg/170px-Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg/255px-Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg/340px-Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="889" data-file-height="1334" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_Graham_Bell.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>engineering scientists</b> including <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Graham_Bell" title="Alexander Graham Bell">Alexander Graham Bell</a> (inventor of the telephone),<sup id="cite_ref-tele20612_312-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele20612-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francis_Crick" title="Francis Crick">Francis Crick</a> (co-discoverer of the structure of DNA),<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hans_Eysenck" title="Hans Eysenck">Hans Eysenck</a> (psychologist who created the modern scientific theory of personality),<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Ambrose_Fleming" title="John Ambrose Fleming">John Ambrose Fleming</a> (inventor of the vacuum tube), <a href="/wiki/Jaroslav_Heyrovsk%C3%BD" title="Jaroslav Heyrovský">Jaroslav Heyrovský</a> (father of the electroanalytical method) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kuen_Kao" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Kuen Kao">Charles Kuen Kao</a> (pioneer of the use of fibre optics in telecommunications);,<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Prell" title="Donald Prell">Donald Prell</a> (psychologist and <a href="/wiki/Futurologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Futurologist">Futurologist</a>).</li>
<li><b>entertainers, musicians, composers and filmmakers</b> including <a href="/wiki/Ken_Adam" title="Ken Adam">Ken Adam</a> (designer famous for set designs for the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_films" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond films">James Bond films</a>), <a href="/wiki/Brett_Anderson" title="Brett Anderson">Brett Anderson</a> (lead singer of the band <a href="/wiki/Suede_(band)" title="Suede (band)">Suede</a>), <a href="/wiki/Justine_Frischmann" title="Justine Frischmann">Justine Frischmann</a> (lead singer of the band <a href="/wiki/Elastica" title="Elastica">Elastica</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a> (comedian and actor),<sup id="cite_ref-tele20612_312-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele20612-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Holst" title="Gustav Holst">Gustav Holst</a> (composer), all of the members of the band <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Buckland" title="Jonny Buckland">Jonny Buckland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_Berryman" title="Guy Berryman">Guy Berryman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will_Champion" title="Will Champion">Will Champion</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a> (director of films including <i>The Dark Knight saga</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Franny_Armstrong" title="Franny Armstrong">Franny Armstrong</a> (director), <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice-Oxley" title="Tim Rice-Oxley">Tim Rice-Oxley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hughes_(musician)" title="Richard Hughes (musician)">Richard Hughes</a> (members of the band <a href="/wiki/Keane_(band)" title="Keane (band)">Keane</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Ross_(television_presenter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jonathan Ross (television presenter)">Jonathan Ross</a> (television presenter);</li>
<li><b>journalists and commentators</b> including <a href="/wiki/A._A._Gill" title="A. A. Gill">A. A. Gill</a> (columnist), three former editors of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, most notably <a href="/wiki/Walter_Bagehot" title="Walter Bagehot">Walter Bagehot</a>, two editors of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_Literary_Supplement" title="The Times Literary Supplement">The Times Literary Supplement</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Dimbleby" title="Jonathan Dimbleby">Jonathan Dimbleby</a> (television and radio current affairs presenter),<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Dyckhoff" title="Tom Dyckhoff">Tom Dyckhoff</a> (architecture critic and TV presenter),<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> former ITN Home Affairs Correspondent <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Cullen" title="Sarah Cullen">Sarah Cullen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Inglis" title="Simon Inglis">Simon Inglis</a> (architectural historian and sports writer);<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>politicians</b> including <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> (leader of the Indian independence movement),<sup id="cite_ref-tele20612_312-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele20612-312">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jomo_Kenyatta" title="Jomo Kenyatta">Jomo Kenyatta</a> (first Prime Minister, first President and "Father of the Nation" of Kenya),<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a> (first Prime Minister, President and "Founder" of Ghana and "Father" of African Nationalism),<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a> (first Prime Minister and "Father of the Nation" of Mauritius),<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chaim_Herzog" title="Chaim Herzog">Chaim Herzog</a> (former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Israel" title="President of Israel">President of Israel</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sir_Abubakar_Tafawa_Balewa" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Abubakar Tafawa Balewa">Sir Abubakar Tafawa Balewa</a> (first Prime Minister of Nigeria),<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/It%C5%8D_Hirobumi" title="Itō Hirobumi">Itō Hirobumi</a> (first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Japan" title="Prime Minister of Japan">Prime Minister of Japan</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Junichiro_Koizumi" title="Junichiro Koizumi">Junichiro Koizumi</a> (former Prime Minister of Japan),<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wu_Tingfang" title="Wu Tingfang">Wu Tingfang</a> (Acting Premier during the early years of the Republic of China), and <a href="/wiki/Sir_Stafford_Cripps" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Stafford Cripps">Sir Stafford Cripps</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a>);</li>
<li><b>lawyers</b> including a Lord Chancellor (<a href="/wiki/Lord_Herschell" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Herschell">Lord Herschell</a>); Chief Justices of England (<a href="/wiki/Lord_Woolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Woolf">Lord Woolf</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> Hong Kong (Sir <a href="/wiki/William_Meigh_Goodman" class="mw-redirect" title="William Meigh Goodman">William Meigh Goodman</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Yang_Ti-liang" title="Yang Ti-liang">Yang Ti-liang</a>), the British Supreme Court for China and Japan (Sir <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_John_Hannen" title="Nicholas John Hannen">Nicholas John Hannen</a>), India (<a href="/wiki/A._S._Anand" class="mw-redirect" title="A. S. Anand">A. S. Anand</a>), Malaysia (<a href="/wiki/Arifin_Zakaria" title="Arifin Zakaria">Arifin Zakaria</a>), Nigeria (<a href="/wiki/Samuel_Eson_Johnson_Ecoma" title="Samuel Eson Johnson Ecoma">Samuel Eson Johnson Ecoma</a>), Ghana (<a href="/wiki/Samuel_Azu_Crabbe" title="Samuel Azu Crabbe">Samuel Azu Crabbe</a>), The Straits Settlements (Sir <a href="/wiki/G._Aubrey_Goodman" title="G. Aubrey Goodman">G. Aubrey Goodman</a>) and the Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court (Rt. Hon. Sir <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Floissac" title="Vincent Floissac">Vincent Floissac</a>); two Masters of the Rolls (<a href="/wiki/Herbert_Cozens-Hardy,_1st_Baron_Cozens-Hardy" title="Herbert Cozens-Hardy, 1st Baron Cozens-Hardy">Lord Cozens-Hardy</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Jessel_(jurist)" title="George Jessel (jurist)">George Jessel</a>); and Attorneys-General of England (<a href="/wiki/Lord_Goldsmith" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Goldsmith">Lord Goldsmith</a><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Baroness_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Baroness Scotland">Baroness Scotland</a>), Singapore (<a href="/wiki/Tan_Boon_Teik" title="Tan Boon Teik">Tan Boon Teik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chao_Hick_Tin" title="Chao Hick Tin">Chao Hick Tin</a>), Hong Kong (<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chisholm_Anstey" title="Thomas Chisholm Anstey">Thomas Chisholm Anstey</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hassan_Bubacar_Jallow" title="Hassan Bubacar Jallow">Hassan Bubacar Jallow</a>);</li>
<li><b>sports people</b> including <a href="/wiki/David_Gower" title="David Gower">David Gower</a> (former captain of the England cricket team),<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Head" title="Patrick Head">Patrick Head</a> (co-founder of the Williams Formula One team)<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Christine_Ohuruogu" title="Christine Ohuruogu">Christine Ohuruogu</a> (Olympic and World <a href="/wiki/400_metres" title="400 metres">400 metres</a> gold medalist);<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> and</li>
<li><b>statisticians</b> including <a href="/wiki/Karl_Pearson" title="Karl Pearson">Karl Pearson</a> (founder of the world's first university statistics department at UCL)<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kirstine_Smith" title="Kirstine Smith">Kirstine Smith</a> (credited with the creation of <a href="/wiki/Optimal_design" title="Optimal design">optimal design</a> of experiments).<sup id="cite_ref-GL2009_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GL2009-338">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_College_London&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The title of third-oldest university in England is claimed by three institutions: Durham University as the third-oldest officially recognised university (1832) and the third to confer degrees (1837), the University of London as the third university to be granted a Royal Charter (1836), and University College London as it was founded as London University (1826) and was the third-oldest university institution to start teaching (1828). A fourth institution, King's College London, officially claims to be the fourth-oldest university in England; it was the third university institution to receive a Royal Charter (1829) and some claim it as third oldest on that basis. Deciding which is the "third oldest university" depends largely on the definition of university status.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bristol" title="University of Bristol">University of Bristol</a> also makes this claim, having admitted women from its foundation (as a college) in 1876.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Universities practice different methods for counting Nobel prize affiliates, from the flattering to the highly conservative. As of March 2016, UCL had an "official count" of 29 Nobel affiliates as students or academics, and a further 11 as honorary graduates or honorary fellows.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-130"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-130">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Institute of Education (IOE) merged with UCL in December 2014. In the year ended 31 July 2013 the IOE had a total income of £71.42 million and total expenditure of £69.97 million. The IOE had total net assets of £105.17 million at 31 July 2013.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-193"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-193">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">New <a href="/wiki/UCAS" title="UCAS">UCAS</a> points from 2016</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
